Taharah — Purification
intermediate
6 min
Madmadah and Istinshaq: Sunnah Rulings and the New Water Dispute
Inter-madhhab dispute on water use in madmadah and istinshaq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on madmadah and istinshaq, explain the dispute with al-Shafi'i regarding new water, and apply the rule in a scenario with limited water.

Core Idea
Madmadah and istinshaq are sunnah mu'akkadah; Hanafis require new water each cycle; Shafi'is allow one water.

This lesson examines the rulings of rinsing the mouth (madmadah) and sniffing water (istinshaq) in wudu and ghusl according to the Hanafi school. While both acts are sunnah mu'akkadah, there are detailed conditions regarding the number of times and the use of water. We will explore the inter-madhhab dispute with the Shafi'i school on whether new water must be taken for each cycle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their ruling
Identify madmadah and istinshaq as sunnah mu'akkadah in both wudu and ghusl. Note that sin may be incurred if omitted, as they are emphasized sunnah.
The passage explicitly states based on al-Siraj that leaving them incurs sin, aligning with the strength of sunnah mu'akkadah.
2
Note consensus elements
There is consensus (ijma') on two points: giving precedence to madmadah over istinshaq, and performing each act three times (tathlith).
3
Locate the dispute with al-Shafi'i on new water
The Hanafi school holds it is sunnah to take new water for each cycle of madmadah and istinshaq, while al-Shafi'i permits using the same water for all cycles.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf: a Hanafi must use separate water; a Shafi'i may use one water.
4
Examine the Hanafi dalil
The primary proof is the hadith of al-Tabarani: 'He rinsed his mouth three times and sniffed three times, taking new water each time.' Abu Dawud narrated it and remained silent, indicating it is hasan according to al-Nawawi. This explicit evidence outweighs general reports.
5
Apply the ruling to a water shortage scenario
If water is limited such that one can either do ghusl once with madmadah and istinshaq or three times without them, the Hanafi position is to perform ghusl once with both acts, because the Prophet never omitted madmadah and istinshaq, whereas he omitted tathlith on occasion.
This is derived from the teacher's comment in the passage.

Source Text

لصيرورة الماء مستعملاً، ولا يخفى أن نفي الجواز في المسألتين بمعنى نفي الإجزاء في تحصيل السنة لا بمعنى الحرمة لما أن أصلهما سنة، أو تحمل على المضمضة والاستنشاق في الغسل الواجب وقالوا المضمضة والاستنشاق قدمناه أن المواظبة من غير ترك لا تفيد الوجوب وجميع من حكى وضوءه عليه السلام اثنان وعشرون صحابياً كلهم ذكروهما فيه كما في فتح القدير. وفي نسخة شرح عليها مسكين غسل فمه وأنفه بمياه وقال : قوله بمياه جديداً ورواه أبو داود وسكت فكان حجة . وما ورد مما ظاهره المخالفة فمحمول على الموافقة كما في فتح القدير. وفي السراج الوهاج : ولو تمضمض ثلاثاً من غرفة واحدة لم يصر آتياً أي بأن استنشق ببعضه وتمضمض بالباقي . قوله : (قال أستاذنا يتبين من هذا الخ) هو من كلام المعراج . ثم أن الإشارة في قوله من هذا لا يظهر رجوعها إلى قوله ترك التكرار لا يكره أي تكرار المضمضة والاستنشاق كما لا يخفى، بل هو راجع إلى كونهما سنتين مؤكدتين بأثم بتركهما . وعبارة المعراج نصها هكذا : وفي الشفاء المضمضة والاستنشاق سنتان مؤكدتان من تركهما يأثم. وفي مبسوط شيخ الإسلام ترك التكرار لا يكره مع الإمكان. قال أستاذنا : يتبين من هذا الخ. قوله: (يغسل مرة معهما) أي لأن النبي ورد عنه ترك التثليث حيث غسل مرة مرة وقال : «هذا وضوء لا يقبل الله الصلاة إلا به ولم يرد عنه ترك المضمضة والاستنشاق كما سيأتي . قوله : ورواه أبو داود وسكت أنه بالسنة. وذكر الصيرفي آتياً بالسنة ا.هـ. ولا يخفى أنه يكون آتياً بسنة المضمضة لا يصير بسنة كونها ثلاثاً بمياه فالنفي والإثبات في القولين بالاعتبارين فلا اختلاف.
The book of purification. Regarding the water becoming used: it is not hidden that the negation of permissibility in the two issues means negation of validity in attaining the sunnah, not prohibition, because their origin is sunnah. Or it is interpreted concerning madmadah and istinshaq in obligatory ghusl. They said: madmadah and istinshaq are two sunans that include other sunan: from them is giving precedence to madmadah over istinshaq by consensus, and from them is repetition (tathlith) for each one by consensus, and taking new water in the repetition is sunnah in our school, while al-Shafi'i holds it with one water. Taking new water for each of the two is sunnah in our school, while al-Shafi'i holds that they have one water. Removing mucus with the left hand. As mentioned in al-Mi'raj. In al-Bada'i' and al-Mabsut: performing both with the right hand is sunnah. In al-Munyah: he sniffs with the left. In al-Mi'raj: leaving repetition is not disliked if possible. Our teacher said: from this it appears that if one has water sufficient for ghusl once with madmadah and istinshaq, or three times without them, he should wash once with them. In al-Siraj: they are two emphasized sunans; indeed, leaving madmadah and istinshaq incurs sin according to the correct view. It is not hidden that sin is attached to leaving an obligatory act, and the answer can be from what they said: the emphasized sunnah is in the strength of obligatory. The proof of their being sunnah is the constant practice (muwazabah) as in al-Hidayah. In Ghayat al-Bayan: meaning with occasional omission, otherwise they would be obligatory. And you have learned from what we presented that constant practice without omission does not necessitate obligation. All who narrated his wudu, peace be upon him, are twenty-two Companions; all of them mentioned them in it, as in Fath al-Qadir. In a copy with a commentary by Miskin: 'He washed his mouth and nose with waters' and said: the phrase 'with waters' belongs to each one. And what is in al-Wafi: 'He washed his mouth with waters and his nose with waters' is better than what is in al-Kanz to indicate renewal of water in each of them. And it has come explicitly in the hadith of al-Tabarani from his saying: 'He rinsed his mouth three times and sniffed three times, taking new water each time.' And Abu Dawud narrated it and remained silent, so it was a proof. And what has come that apparently contradicts it is interpreted in agreement, as in Fath al-Qadir. And in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: if one rinses three times from one handful, he does not fulfill [the sunnah], meaning that he sniffs with part and rinses with the remainder. His saying: (Our teacher said: from this it becomes clear etc.) is from the speech of al-Mi'raj. Then the reference in 'from this' apparently does not refer to his saying 'leaving repetition is not disliked' meaning repetition of madmadah and istinshaq, as is not hidden, but rather refers to them being two emphasized sunans with sin for leaving them. The text of al-Mi'raj is verbatim: 'In al-Shifa: madmadah and istinshaq are two emphasized sunans; whoever leaves them sins.' And in Mabsut of Shaykh al-Islam: 'Leaving repetition is not disliked if possible.' Our teacher said: from this it becomes clear etc. His saying: ('he washes once with them') meaning because it is narrated from the Prophet that he left tathlith, where he washed once and said: 'This is wudu without which Allah does not accept prayer.' And it is not narrated from him that he left madmadah and istinshaq, as will come. His saying: ('And Abu Dawud narrated it and remained silent about it') Imam al-Nawawi said in his abridgement called al-Taqrib: 'Among the sources of hasan is Sunan Abi Dawud, for he mentions in it the sahih and what resembles it and is close to it, and what is severely weak he clarifies. And what he does not mention anything about is sound. Thus, what we find in his book absolutely, and no other reliable scholar has authenticated or weakened it, it is hasan according to Abu Dawud.' End. 'That it is sunnah.' And al-Sayrafi mentioned: 'He is performer of the sunnah.' End. And it is not hidden that he is performer of the sunnah of madmadah but does not become performer of the sunnah of it being three times with waters. So negating and affirming in the two statements are from two considerations, so there is no contradiction.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage deals with the rulings of madmadah (rinsing the mouth) and istinshaq (sniffing water into the nose) during wudu and ghusl. The author begins by explaining that the negation of permissibility regarding using water that has become musta'mal (used) means negation of validity in attaining the sunnah, not prohibition, since the original act is sunnah. Then it discusses the various sunan within madmadah and istinshaq: the order (madmadah before istinshaq by consensus), repetition (three times each by consensus), taking new water for each cycle (in our Hanafi school, it is sunnah to take new water each time; al-Shafi'i holds it can be done with one water), and using the left hand to remove mucus. The author cites sources like Al-Mi'raj, Al-Bada'i', Al-Mabsut, and Al-Munyah. There is discussion on the status: according to Al-Siraj, they are sunnah mu'akkadah such that leaving them incurs sin according to the correct view. But sin is normally linked to leaving a wajib, so they explain that sunnah mu'akkadah is in the strength of wajib. The proof of their sunnah status is the Prophet's constant practice (muwazabah) with occasional omission. The author notes that 22 Companions narrated the Prophet's wudu and all mentioned madmadah and istinshaq. The hadith of al-Tabarani explicitly mentions taking new water each time, and Abu Dawud recorded it as a proof. The commentary then clarifies that if one cannot do both three times due to limited water, one should perform madmadah and istinshaq once rather than omit them entirely. The passage also addresses the grading of the hadith: al-Nawawi said that Abu Dawud's silence indicates the hadith is hasan. Finally, the author reconciles apparent contradictions: performing madmadah and istinshaq with one water still fulfills the sunnah of the act but not the sunnah of tathlith with new water; thus the two statements (negation and affirmation) are about different aspects, so no contradiction.

Key Terms
مضمضة (madmadah): Rinsing the mouth with water during wudu or ghusl
استنشاق (istinshaq): Sniffing water into the nose and expelling it during wudu or ghusl
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah mu'akkadah): An emphasized sunnah that the Prophet consistently performed; leaving it is disliked and may incur sin
مواظبة (muwazabah): The Prophet's continuous practice of an act without abandoning it

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on taking new water for each cycle of madmadah and istinshaq?
A) Sunnah mu'akkadah
B) Wajib
C) Mustahab
D) Makruh

Key Takeaway
Madmadah and istinshaq are sunnah mu'akkadah; the Hanafi school requires new water for each cycle based on an explicit hadith, and in case of water shortage, performing them once is better than omitting them.

The Ruling on Khilal of the Beard and Fingers in Wudu
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sunnah vs mustahabb for beard; unanimous sunnah for fingers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on khilal of the beard and fingers, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the beard's status.

Core Idea
Khilal of the beard is sunnah on the most correct view; Abu Hanifa held it mustahabb; khilal of fingers is sunnah by agreement.

This passage from Bahr al-Raiq addresses the practice of passing water through the beard and between the fingers during wudu. While the fingers are unanimously considered sunnah, the beard involves a nuanced disagreement within the Hanafi school between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to differentiate between sunnah and mustahabb, and to appreciate how proofs are weighed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the two positions
The act is khilal (passing water through) of the beard and fingers. For the beard, Abu Hanifa says mustahabb; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say sunnah. For the fingers, all agree it is sunnah.
The text explicitly labels the beard dispute as intra-Hanafi.
2
Examine the proofs for each position
Abu Hanifa's evidence: lack of proven continuous practice (muwazabah) and the beard not being the place of obligation. The other view's proof: Hadith of Anas where the Prophet took water under his chin and passed it through his beard, saying 'My Lord commanded me to do this.'
This hadith is cited as authentic (Sunan Abi Dawud).
3
Understand the rebuttal and the resolution
The text rebuts Abu Hanifa's objections: the hadith is authentic and its command implies continuity; the 'inside of the beard' objection is overruled by the explicit hadith. The dispute is resolved in favour of sunnah based on the hadith and the collective reasoning of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.
Al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah confirms the relied-upon view as sunnah.
4
Apply the principle to the fingers
For the fingers, the proof is the hadith of Laqeet ibn Sabrah: 'When you perform wudu, complete the wudu and pass water between your fingers.' This is unanimous sunnah.
The fingers include both hands and feet; the method is using dripping water or immersing in water.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (وتخليل لحيته وأصابعه أما تخليل اللحية وهو تفريق الشعر من جهة الأسفل إلى فوق لغير المحرم فسنة على الأصح ، وقيده في السراج الوهاج بأن يكون بماء متقاطر في تخليل الأصابع ولم يقيده في تخليل اللحية. وهل قول أبي يوسف وحده أو معه محمد؟ قولان ذكرهما في المعراج وصحح في خير مطلوب أن محمداً مع أبي يوسف. وعند أبي حنيفة مستحب لعدم ثبوت المواظبة ولأن السنة إكمال الفرض في محله وداخل اللحية ليس بمحل الفرض لعدم وجوب إيصال الماء إلى الشعر. وجه الأصح ما رواه أبو داود عن أنس : كان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم إذ توضأ أخذ كفاً ماء تحت حنكه فخلل به لحيته وقال : بهذا أمرني وكذا المنذري بعده وهو مغن عن نقل صريح المواظبة لأن أمره حامل عليها. وقولهم داخل اللحية ليس بمحل الفرض ممنوع بعد ثبوت الحديث الصحيح بخلافه، وما أورد عليه أن المضمضة والاستنشاق سنتان أنهما ليستا في محل الفرض أجيب عنه بأنهما في الوجه وهو محل الفرض إذ لهما حكم الخارج من وجه ولأن الكلام في سنة تكون تبعاً للفرض بقرينة المقام وإلا يخرج عنه بعض السنن كالنية والتسمية كما لا يخفى . وإنما لم يكن التخليل واجباً بالأمر في أمرني ربي) وخللوا أصابعكم الآتي لوجود الصارف وهو تعليم الأعرابي والأخبار التي حكى فيها وضوء رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فإن التخليل لم يذكر فيها، وما في أنا لو قلنا بالوجوب لزم الزيادة على النص بخبر الواحد فيه كلام إذ لا يلزم إلا لو قلنا بالافتراض. وما في الكافي من أنا لو قلنا بالوجوب في الوضوء لساوى التبع الأصل ضعيف، ولأنه لا مانع منه إذا اقتضاه الدليل لأن ثبوت الحكم بقدر دليله. ولأنه قد ظهر عدم المساواة في حكم آخر وهو كونه لا يلزم بالنذر بخلاف الصلاة وأما تخليل الأصابع فهو إدخال بعضها في بعض بماء متقاطر ويقوم مقامه الإدخال في الماء، ولو لم يكن جارياً فسنة اتفاقاً أعني أصابع اليدين والرجلين لما في السنن الأربعة في حديث لقيط ابن صبرة قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إذا توضأت فأسبغ الوضوء وخلل بين الأصابع (۱) قال الترمذي حديث
النهاية من وبسنة
قوله: (لا بسنة كونها ثلاثاً بمياه النفي باعتبار القيد الأخير أي يكون آتياً بسنة المضمضة ) التثليث أيضاً دون سنة تجديد الماء في كل مرة. قوله : (ولم يقيده في تخليل اللحية سيأتي) في الحديث أنه أخذ كفاً . من ماء. قوله : (وهل هو ) أي القول بالسنية الذي هو الأصح قوله : (بعد ثبوت الحديث الصحيح بخلافه أي بخلاف ما أفاده قولهم داخل اللحية الخ. قوله : (وما أورد عليه) أي على
His saying: (And passing water through his beard and fingers). As for passing water through the beard, which is separating the hair from the bottom upward for one not in ihram, it is sunnah on the most correct view. Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj restricted it to being with dripping water in the case of the fingers, but did not restrict it in the case of the beard. And whether it is the saying of Abu Yusuf alone or with Muhammad? There are two opinions mentioned in al-Mi'raj, and it was confirmed in Khayr Matlub that Muhammad is with Abu Yusuf. And according to Abu Hanifa, it is mustahabb due to lack of proven continuous practice, and because the sunnah is completion of the obligation in its place, and the inside of the beard is not the place of the obligation due to not being required to reach water to the hair. The proof of the correct view is what Abu Dawud narrated from Anas: 'When the Prophet performed wudu, he took a handful of water under his chin and passed it through his beard, and said: 'My Lord commanded me to do this.'' And al-Mundhiri is after him, and it suffices instead of explicit transmission of continuous practice because the command implies it. And their saying that the inside of the beard is not the place of the obligation is rejected after the establishment of the authentic hadith contrary to it. And what is objected to it, that madmadah and istinshaq are sunnah even though they are not in the place of obligation, is answered by saying that they are on the face, which is the place of obligation, because they have the ruling of being external from the face. And because the discussion is about a sunnah that is a follower of the obligation by context, otherwise some sunan would be excluded, like intention and tasmiyah, as is not hidden. And passing water through the beard did not become obligatory by the command in 'My Lord commanded me' and 'Pass water between your fingers' to come, due to the presence of a diverting factor, which is the teaching of the Bedouin and the reports that narrated the wudu of the Messenger of Allah, in which passing through the beard was not mentioned. And what is in al-Kafi: 'If we said it is obligatory in wudu, the follower would equal the original' is weak, because there is no prevention if the evidence requires it, because the ruling is established by the extent of its proof. And because it has become clear that there is no equality in another ruling, which is that it is not binding by vow, unlike prayer. As for passing water through the fingers, it is inserting some into others with dripping water, and inserting into water takes its place. And if there is no running water, it is sunnah by agreement, meaning the fingers of the hands and feet, due to what is in the four Sunan in the hadith of Laqeet ibn Sabrah: 'The Messenger of Allah said: When you perform wudu, complete the wudu and pass water between the fingers.' At-Tirmidhi said: hasan hadith. End of the main text. And the marginal notes: 'From the end of the text and with sunnah.' 'His saying: (Not with the sunnah of it being three times with waters) the negation is with consideration of the last restriction, meaning he becomes performer of the sunnah of madmadah and tathlith also without the sunnah of renewing water each time. His saying: (And he did not restrict it in the case of the beard will come) in the hadith that he took a handful of water. His saying: (And whether it is) meaning the saying of it being sunnah which is the most correct. His saying: (After the establishment of the authentic hadith contrary to it) i.e. contrary to what their saying 'inside the beard' indicates. His saying: (And what is objected to it) i.e. upon'
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage deals with khilal of the beard and fingers during wudu. For the beard, the relied-upon view is that it is sunnah for one not in ihram, defined as parting the hair from the bottom upward using water. The author mentions that Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj specified that for the fingers, the water should be dripping, but did not specify that for the beard. There is a dispute: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold it is sunnah, while Abu Hanifa holds it is mustahabb due to lack of proven continuous practice and because the inside of the beard is not the prescribed place for the obligation of wudu. The proof for sunnah is the hadith of Anas where the Prophet took a handful of water under his chin and passed it through his beard, saying 'My Lord commanded me to do this.' The response to Abu Hanifa's objection that the beard is not a place of obligation is rebutted by the authentic hadith. Additionally, it is argued that the inside of the beard is like the face, as madmadah and istinshaq are sunnah even though they are within the face. The passage also explains why khilal is not wajib despite the command: the command is understood as instructional rather than obligatory, and the reports describing the Prophet's wudu do not mention khilal. For the fingers, the ruling is sunnah by agreement, supported by the hadith of Laqeet ibn Sabrah: 'When you perform wudu, complete the wudu and pass water between your fingers.' This applies to fingers of hands and feet.

Key Terms
تخليل (takhleel): Passing water through or between something, such as the beard or fingers, during wudu
لحية (lihyah): The beard, specifically the hair on the chin and cheeks
مستحب (mustahabb): Recommended but not obligatory; leaving it is not sinful

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Khilal of the beard is sunnah on the relied-upon view, while khilal of the fingers is sunnah by agreement; a command in a hadith can be diverted from obligation by contextual factors.

The Ruling and Method of Khilal in Wudu
Analyzing the legal status of khilal as sunnah and describing its prophetic method.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of khilal in wudu and explain why the Hanafi school classifies it as sunnah despite the apparent command.

Core Idea
Khilal is sunnah, not wajib, because the hadith's threat is conditional and its transmission is weak.

The practice of running water between the fingers and toes (khilal) is a well-known sunnah in wudu. However, some might think it is obligatory due to a hadith that contains a threat. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi reasoning that clarifies why it remains a recommended act, not a required one.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is khilal (running water between fingers and toes). The Hanafi ruling is sunnah (recommended).
Sunnah here means a recommended practice that the Prophet regularly performed.
2
Locate the dalil
The main proof cited is the hadith from al-Darqutni: 'Khallilu asabi'akum la yutakhallilaha Allahu bi al-nar...' (Put water between your fingers, lest Allah put fire between them).
This is an ahad hadith, not mutawatir.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'khallilu' suggests a command, but in Hanafi usul, a command from an ahad hadith does not confer obligation (wujub) when there is a preventive factor (sarf). Here, the threat is conditional and the hadith is weak, so it only indicates recommendation.
The logical analysis shows the threat does not necessarily apply to omission of khilal.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some may consider khilal wajib based on the apparent command. The Hanafi response is that the threat is not unconditional and the hadith is weak, so it remains sunnah.
This ikhtilaf is not a major madhhab dispute; it is a matter of usul interpretation.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that khilal is sunnah, as stated in al-Zahiriyyah and Fath al-Qadir.
The tarjih is based on the weakness of the hadith and the logical defect in the threat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حسن صحيح. وتقدم الصارف له عن الوجوب . وكذا ما رواه الدارقطني «خللوا أصابعكم لا يتخللها الله بالنار يوم القيامة لأنه ليس فيه الوعيد على الترك حتى يفيد الوجوب لأن منطوقه أن تخليل الأصابع في الوضوء يراد لعدم تخللها نار جهنم وهو لا يستلزم أن عدم التخليل في الوضوء يستلزم تخلل النار إلا لو كان تخليل الأصابع في الوضوء علة مساوية لعدم تخليلها بالنار وهو منتف بأنه قد يوجد التخليل بالنار. مع تخليل الأصابع، فحينئذ لا حاجة إلى ما ذكر في شروح الهداية من أن الوعيد مصروف إلى ما إذا لم يصل الماء إلى ما بين الأصابع إذ قد علمت أنه لا وعيد في الحديث هذا مع أن ما قالوه لا يتم لأنه إذا لم يصل يكون الغسل فرضاً وليس التخليل غسلاً كما لا يخفى هذا مع أن حديث الدارقطني ضعيف كما في فتح القدير. وفي الظهيرية والتخليل إنما يكون بعد التثليث لأنه سنة التثليث . ثم قيل : الأولى في أصابع اليدين أن يكون تخليلها بالتشبيك، وصفته في الرجلين أن يخلل بخنصر يده اليسرى خنصر رجله اليمنى ويختم بخنصر رجله اليسرى كذلك ورد الخبر. كذا في معراج الدراية وغيره وتعقبه في فتح القدير بقوله والله أعلم به، ومثله فيما يظهر أمر اتفاقي لا سنة مقصودة ا هـ . لكن ورد بعض هذه الكيفية فيما رواه ابن ماجه عن المستورد بن شداد قال : رأيت رسول الله لا يتوضأ فخلل أصابع رجليه بخنصره. وأما كونه بخنصر يده اليسرى وبكونه من أسفل فالله أعلم .به ويشكل كونه بخنصر اليسرى أن من الطهارة المستحب في فعلها أن تكون باليمين ولعل الحكمة في كونها بالخنصر كونها أدق الأصابع فهي بالتخليل أنسب كذا في شرح المنية. وقولهم من أسفل إلى فوق يحتمل شيئين: أحدهما أنه يبدأ من أسفل الأصابع إلى فوق من ظهر القدم. ثانيهما أن يكون المراد من أسفل الأصبع من باطن القدم كما جزم به في السراج الوهاج والأول أقرب. وفي المعراج عن شيخه العلامة في قوله عليه السلام خللوا الحديث دليل على أن وظيفة الرجل الغسل لا المسح فكان حجة على الروافض ا هـ .
Hasan sahih. And the preventive factor from obligation has been discussed. Likewise, what al-Darqutni narrated: 'Put water between your fingers, lest Allah put fire between them on the Day of Resurrection' because there is no threat of leaving it to indicate obligation, since its literal sense is that putting water between fingers in wudu is intended to avoid fire between them on the Day of Resurrection, and it does not necessitate that not doing so entails fire, unless the cause [of fire] is exactly the opposite of doing so, which is not the case, because fire may occur even with doing so. Therefore, there is no need for what is mentioned in the commentaries of al-Hidayah that the threat applies when water does not reach between the fingers, since we know there is no threat in this hadith. Moreover, what they say is not complete, because if water does not reach, washing is obligatory, and khilal is not washing, as is clear. Additionally, the hadith of al-Darqutni is weak as in Fath al-Qadir. In al-Zahiriyyah: Khilal is only done after the third wash because it is the sunnah of the third wash. Then it is said: The best for the fingers of the hands is to do khilal by interlacing (tashbik); and for the feet, by using the little finger of the left hand to do khilal of the little toe of the right foot, and ending with the little toe of the left foot. Thus it is reported. This is in Mi'raj al-Dirayah and others, but it is contested in Fath al-Qadir by saying: Allah knows best, and this appears to be an incidental matter, not an intended sunnah. However, some of this manner is reported in what Ibn Majah narrated from al-Mustawrid ibn Shaddad: 'I saw the Messenger of Allah perform wudu and do khilal of his toes with his little finger.' As for using the left hand's little finger and doing it from below, Allah knows best. The use of the left little finger is problematic because it is recommended in purification to use the right hand. Perhaps the wisdom in using the little finger is that it is the thinnest, so it is most suitable for khilal, as in Sharh al-Munyah. Their saying 'from below to above' can mean two things: (1) starting from the bottom of the toes upward on the top of the foot; (2) meaning from beneath the toes on the sole of the foot, as stated in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj; the first is closer. In al-Mi'raj from his teacher the Allamah: The Prophet's saying 'do khilal' indicates that the function of the foot in wudu is washing, not wiping, so it is a proof against the Rafidah.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the ruling of khilal (running water between the fingers and toes) in wudu. The author begins by citing the hadith from al-Darqutni and clarifies that despite its apparent threat, khilal is not wajib but sunnah. The reason is that the threat is conditioned on a cause that may not be present; moreover, the hadith is weak. The commentator then explains the preferred method: for hands, by interlacing (tashbik); for feet, using the left pinky finger, starting from the bottom of the toes. There is some disagreement on the exact method, but the principle is that it is not a fixed sunnah but rather a recommended practice. The passage concludes by noting that the hadith is also used to refute the Rafidah who hold that feet are only wiped in wudu, as the command to do khilal implies washing.

Key Terms
التخليل (al-takhli): Running water between the fingers or toes with the finger of the hand
التشبيك (al-tashbik): Interlacing the fingers of both hands to pass water between them

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling of khilal (passing fingers between toes) in wudu?
A) Fard (obligatory)
B) Wajib (necessary)
C) Sunnah (recommended)
D) Mubah (permissible)

Key Takeaway
Khilal is a sunnah act in wudu, and its omission does not affect the validity of wudu.

The Ruling on Washing Each Limb Three Times in Wudu
Explaining the sunnah nature of washing three times and the issue of sin for leaving the extra washes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on washing each limb three times in wudu and evaluate the differing opinions on whether sin is incurred for leaving the extra washes.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, the first wash is fard; the next two are sunnah mu'akkadah; leaving them is not sinful unless habitual.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies the legal status of washing each limb multiple times in wudu. While many Muslims assume three washes are required, the Hanafi school distinguishes between the obligatory first wash and the recommended second and third. The text also addresses a common point of confusion: whether leaving the extra washes constitutes a sin. The preferred position is that it does not, based on careful interpretation of prophetic hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what exactly is being ruled upon (washing each limb in wudu) and what the Hanafi position is: first wash is fard, second and third are sunnah mu'akkadah.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the evidence cited: the hadith where the Prophet performed one, two, and three washes and said 'This is my wudu.'
This hadith is narrated by al-Darqutni, Ibn Majah, and al-Nasa'i.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the hadith proves the ruling: the Prophet's action shows the sunnah, and his statement 'this is my wudu' establishes three as the complete practice.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute: some scholars say sin is incurred for leaving the extra washes; others say no sin. The text also discusses the interpretation of the warning 'whoever increases or decreases.'
The warning is interpreted to refer to belief, not action.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Determine which view is preferred: no sin for leaving the extra washes, especially if not habitual. The threat in the hadith is for those who do not believe the three are sunnah.
Al-Zahiriyyah and al-Hidayah prefer this view.

ربه كذا في الظهيرية، ولا يخفى ترجيح الثاني لقولهم والوعيد في الحديث لعدم رؤيته الثلاث سنة ، فلو كان الإثم يحصل بالترك لما احتيج إلى حمل الحديث على ما ذكروا . وقيل : إن اعتاد يكره وإلا فلا واختاره في الخلاصة. وقد ذكروا دليل السنة أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم توضأ مرة مرة وقال هذا وضوء من لا يقبل الله الصلاة إلا به، وتوضأ مرتين مرتين وقال هذا وضوء من يضاعف الله له الأجر مرتين، وتوضأ ثلاثاً ثلاثاً وقال هذا وضوئي ووضوء الأنبياء من قبلي، فمن زاد على هذا أو نقص فقد تعدى وظلم .. فأما صدره إلى قوله فمن زاد فرواه الدارقطني، وأما عجزه من قوله «فمن زاد» إلى آخره فرواه ابن ماجه والنسائي، وقوله توضأ مرة أي غسل كل عضو مرة، والمراد بالقبول الجواز بمعنى الصحة وإنما قلنا هذا لما عرف أن القبول لا يلازم الصحة لأن الصحة وجود الشرائط والأركان والقبول يعتمد صدق العزيمة وخلوصها. وله شرائط كثيرة لقوله تعالى إنما يتقبل الله من المتقين ﴾ [المائدة: ٢٧]. واختلف في معنى قوله «فمن زاد على هذا على أقوال؛ فقيل على الحد المحدود وهو مردود له عليه الصلاة والسلام من استطاع منكم أن يطيل غرته فليفعل (۲) والحديث لا يلحقه الوعيد كذا في البدائع واقتصر عليه في الهداية. وعلى الأقوال كلها لو زاد لطمأنينة القلب تعتمد فيدخلها من جهة باطن القدم ويصعد بها من أسفل إلى فوق قوله : ( ولا يخفى ترجيح الثاني الخ) قال بعض الفضلاء هذا يخالف ما قاله في المضمضة . من أن السنة المؤكدة في قوة الواجب فيأثم بتركها. وقال في باب صفة الصلاة : اعلم أن الظاهر من كلام أهل المذهب أن الإثم منوط بترك الواجب أو السنة المؤكدة على الصحيح His saying: (And washing three times) i.e., repeating it three times is sunnah, but the first is fard and the two are two emphasized sunnahs. Their saying: Inside the beard is not a place of obligation. His saying: (And it is refuted by the fact that fire may exist with khilal of fingers) contains discussion: because if khilal of fingers in wudu were not a equal cause for lack of fire between them, then the Prophet's saying 'Allah will not put fire between them' would have no benefit, and the attribution of the command for khilal would not be sound, and doing it and not doing it would be equal due to lack of necessity of receiving the promised benefit by doing it and its opposite by leaving it. How can this be when the threat is explicitly stated in the hadith of al-Tabarani as quoted in al-Fath: 'Whoever does not put water between his fingers, Allah will put fire between his fingers on the Day of Resurrection'? So reflect on that. His saying: (from) the top of the foot is attached to 'he begins' i.e., he starts from the direction of the top of the foot, inserting his little finger between the toes and doing khilal from below upwards. As for the second, on the correct view it is as in al-Siraj and chosen in al-Mabsut. The better opinion is to say that they are an emphasized sunnah; the second alone or the third alone is not described as sunnah except with consideration of the other. And the sunnah is repeating the complete washes, not the scoopings. If one is content with one time, it is said he sins because he left the well-known sunnah; it is said he does not sin because he has performed what his Lord commanded him, as in al-Zahiriyyah. And the preference for the second is not hidden, because of their saying: the threat in the hadith is due to not seeing the three as sunnah. So if sin were incurred by leaving, there would be no need to interpret the hadith as they mentioned. And it is said: if he is accustomed, it is disliked, otherwise not, and this is chosen in al-Khulasah. They mentioned the evidence of the sunnah: that the Messenger of Allah performed wudu once and said: 'This is the wudu of one whose prayer Allah does not accept except with it.' He performed wudu twice and said: 'This is the wudu of one whose reward Allah doubles.' He performed wudu three times and said: 'This is my wudu and the wudu of the prophets before me. So whoever increases beyond this or decreases has transgressed and wronged.' The first part up to 'so whoever increases' was narrated by al-Darqutni, and the last part from 'so whoever increases' onward was narrated by Ibn Majah and al-Nasa'i. His saying 'once' means washing each limb once. By 'acceptance' is meant permissibility in the sense of validity. We say this because it is known that acceptance does not entail validity, because validity is the existence of conditions and pillars, while acceptance depends on sincerity and purity of intention. It has many conditions, as Allah says: 'Indeed, Allah only accepts from the righteous' [5:27]. They differed on the meaning of 'whoever increases beyond this' into several opinions: it is said it means the defined limit, and this is rejected because the Prophet said: 'Whoever among you can make his forehead shining, let him do so' – the hadith is in al-Masabih, and making the forehead shining is by increasing beyond the defined limit. It is also said it means the limbs of wudu, and it is said it means increase or decrease in number. The correct view is that it is carried on belief, not the action itself, so that if one increases or decreases but believes that three is sunnah, the threat does not apply to him, as in al-Bada'i' and al-Hidayah. In all opinions, if one increases for tranquility of heart, it is relied upon. Then he inserts it from the direction of the sole of the foot and goes up from below to above. His saying: (And the preference for the second is not hidden, etc.) Some virtuous person said: This contradicts what he said about rinsing the mouth, that the emphasized sunnah is in the strength of wajib, so one sins by leaving it. He said in the chapter on description of prayer: Know that the apparent from the speech of the school's scholars is that sin is attached to leaving a wajib or an emphasized sunnah according to the correct view, due to their explicit statement that whoever leaves the sunnahs of the five prayers – it is said he does not sin, and the correct view is that he does sin. This is mentioned in Fath al-Qadir. And their explicit statement of sin for leaving the congregation even though it is an emphasized sunnah according to the correct view, and similarly in its parallels, as is known to one who traces their speech. And there is no doubt that sin is said by way of gradation, more severe than some; thus the sin for leaving the emphasized sunnah is lighter than the sin for leaving the wajib. And he said in some part of it.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling of washing each limb three times in wudu. The commentator explains that the first wash is fard (obligatory) and the second and third are sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah). There is a difference of opinion on whether one is sinful for leaving the extra washes: some say yes because it is sunnah mu'akkadah, others say no because he has fulfilled the obligation. The preferred view is that he is not sinful, especially if he does not habitually leave it. The hadith where the Prophet performed one, two, and three washes shows the merit of three. The warning 'whoever increases or decreases' is interpreted to refer to belief, not action, meaning that if one believes the three washes are obligatory, he should not add more, but if he does it out of habit, it is permissible. The passage also reconciles apparent contradictions regarding the sin for leaving sunnah mu'akkadah, concluding that sin for leaving an emphasized sunnah is lighter than sin for leaving a wajib.

Key Terms
تثليث الغسل (tathlith al-ghusl): Washing each limb three times in wudu
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah mu'akkadah): Emphasized sunnah; leaving it is disliked but not sinful according to the preferred view, though some scholars say it incurs sin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on washing each limb three times in wudu?
A) The first wash is fard, the second and third are sunnah mu'akkadah
B) All three washes are fard
C) All three washes are sunnah
D) Only one wash is required, three is innovation

Key Takeaway
Washing three times in wudu is a recommended sunnah mu'akkadah, but the obligation is fulfilled with one wash, and leaving the extra washes does not entail sin according to the preferred Hanafi view.

The Sunnah of Washing Three Times in Wudu and the Ruling on Leaving It
Ruling with proof on three washes in wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on washing each limb three times in wudu and explain why leaving it does not incur sin according to the preferred view.

Core Idea
Washing three times is a confirmed sunnah – leaving it is not sinful because the hadith warning is about belief, not the act.

This lesson examines the legal status of washing each limb three times during wudu. While the Prophet consistently performed three washes, the Hanafi school classifies this practice as a confirmed sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah) rather than an obligation. The key question is whether omitting the second and third washes incurs sin. We will explore the hadith evidence and the Hanafi interpretation that resolves the apparent threat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is washing each limb three times in wudu. The Hanafi ruling is sunnah mu'akkadah (confirmed sunnah).
Sunnah mu'akkadah is a category between wajib and mustahabb.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a hadith where the Prophet performed wudu once, twice, and thrice, saying three is his wudu and that of the prophets, and adding: 'Whoever adds or decreases has transgressed and wronged.'
The hadith is narrated by al-Daraqutni, Ibn Majah, and al-Nasa'i.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith shows that one wash is sufficient for validity; three is the complete form. The warning is interpreted as applying to those who believe the number is fixed as obligatory, not to those who omit the extra washes while knowing they are sunnah.
Hanafi usul distinguishes between the act and the belief about it.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some scholars say leaving the sunnah is sinful because it is well-known; the preferred Hanafi view says it is not sinful because one has fulfilled the fard.
The preferred view is supported by al-Hidayah, al-Bada'i', and the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The non-sin view is preferred as it aligns with the principle that sin is attached to abandoning a wajib, not a sunnah. Also, the hadith warning is about belief, not the act.
The author reconciles with other texts by noting varying degrees of emphasis among sunan.

Source Text

باب الإمامة : الجماعة سنة مؤكدة أي قوية تشبه الواجب في القوة والراجح عند أهل المذهب الوجوب، ونقله في البدائع عن عامة مشايخنا، وذكر هو وغيره أن القائل منهم أنها مؤكدة ليس مخالفاً في الحقيقة بل في العبارة لأن السنة والواجب سواء خصوصاً ما كان من شعائر الإسلام اهـ. وفي كلامه تناقض لأنه جعل السنة المؤكدة تارة دون الواجب وتارة مثله ولا يمكن دفعه إلا بحمل أفراد السنة المؤكدة على التفاوت في التأكد والقوة فيكون بعضها لزيادة تأكده في مرتبة الواجب كالجماعة، وبعضها لقلة تأكده دونه كتثليث الغسل قوله : ( فكيف يدعي الاتفاق الخ ) قال في النهر وأقول : لا تدافع في كلامهم لاختلاف الموضوع، وذلك أن ما في الخلاصة فيما إذا أعاده مرة واحدة وما في السراج فيما إذا كرر مراراً. ولفظه في السراج لو تكرر الوضوء في مجلس واحد مراراً لم يستحب بل يكره لما فيه من الإسراف فتدبر اهـ لكن قال الحلبي في شرح المنية : أطبقوا على أن الوضوء عبادة غير مقصودة لذاتها فإذا لم يؤدبه عمل مما هو المقصود من شرعيته كالصلاة وسجد التلاوة ومس أن لا ينبغي يشرع تكراره قربة لكونه غير مقصود لذاته فيكون إسرافاً محضاً اهـ . فليتأمل . قوله : (إذ لا دليل على الكراهة أقول : قد يستدل عليها بالحديث المار من قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «فمن زاد على هذا أو نقص فقد تعدى وظلم لأن أئمتنا استدلوا على أنه مرة واحدة بالحديث المصرح فيه بها وحملوا ما صرح فيه بالثلاث على التثليث بماء واحد كما يأتي فوضوءه عليه السلام ليس فيه تثليث المسح بمياه عندنا فترجع إليه الإشارة في قوله فمن زاد على هذا الخ» إذ لا شك أن هذا زيادة بناء على ما ثبت عندنا من وضوئه تأمل. وفي شرح المنية الكبير بعد حكاية الأقوال ما نصه : والأوجه أنه يكره. قال في الكافي: التثليث يعني بمياه يقربه من الغسل ولو بدله به كره، كذا إذا قربه منه اهـ. قوله : (فلا حاجة حينئذ إلى ما ذكره الزيلعي عبارته هكذا ونيته أي نية الوضوء فالهاء
المصحف
Book of Purification. Page 47. (1) According to the correct view, as in al-Siraj, and he chose it in al-Mabsut.  The more appropriate is to say that they (the second and third washes) are a confirmed sunnah, such that the second alone or the third alone is not described as sunnah except in relation to the other.  The sunnah is the repetition of complete washes, not the repetition of handfuls of water.  If one is content with a single wash, it is said he sins because he abandoned the well-known sunnah, and it is said he does not sin because he has performed what his Lord commanded him, as in al-Zahiriyyah.  The preference for the second is not hidden, due to their statement: 'And the threat in the hadith is because he did not see the three as sunnah.'  If sin occurred by leaving it, there would have been no need to interpret the hadith as they did.  And it is said: if he is accustomed (to leaving it), it is disliked, otherwise not, and he chose this in al-Khulasah.  They have mentioned the proof of the sunnah: that the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, performed wudu once each, saying: 'This is the wudu of one whose prayer Allah does not accept otherwise.'  And he performed wudu twice each, saying: 'This is the wudu of one for whom Allah doubles the reward twice.'  And he performed wudu thrice each, saying: 'This is my wudu and the wudu of the prophets before me.  Whoever adds to this or decreases has transgressed and wronged.'  The first part up to his saying 'faman zad' (whoever adds) was narrated by al-Daraqutni, and the latter part from his saying 'faman zad' to the end was narrated by Ibn Majah and al-Nasa'i.  His saying 'wadda marra' means he washed each limb once.  By 'acceptance' is meant permissibility in the sense of validity.  We said this because it is known that acceptance does not entail validity, because validity is existence of conditions and pillars, while acceptance depends on truthfulness and sincerity of resolve.  It has many conditions due to His statement, the Exalted: 'Allah only accepts from the God-fearing' [al-Ma'idah: 27].  There is disagreement on the meaning of his saying 'faman zad 'ala hadha' (whoever adds to this) among several opinions.  It is said: it means beyond the prescribed limit, and this is rejected because of his statement, peace be upon him: 'Whoever among you can lengthen his blaze, let him do so.' (2) The hadith is in al-Masabih.  Lengthening the blaze is by adding beyond the prescribed limit.  And it is said: it means (adding to) the limbs of wudu.  And it is said: the increase or decrease in number.  The correct opinion is that it is interpreted as referring to belief, not the act itself, so that if one adds or decreases while believing that three is sunnah, the threat does not apply to him, as in al-Bada'i', and al-Hidayah restricted itself to this.  According to all the opinions, if he adds for tranquility of heart...
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage from Sharh al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the ruling on washing each limb three times in wudu. It begins by affirming that the second and third washes are a confirmed sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah) when considered together, not individually. The author prefers this formulation over saying each is sunnah alone. The sunnah is defined as repeating complete washes of the limb, not just scooping water multiple times without covering the whole limb. The main legal question is: if someone washes only once, does he sin? Two views are reported: one says he sins for abandoning a well-known sunnah; the other, considered stronger, says he does not sin because he has fulfilled the obligatory (fard) washing once. The stronger view is supported by the fact that the hadith warning against decreasing is interpreted as referring to belief (that one should consider three as obligatory) rather than the act itself. The author then provides the hadith evidence for the sunnah: the Prophet performed wudu once, twice, and thrice, indicating that one is sufficient for validity, two and three are for increased reward. The hadith 'whoever adds or decreases has transgressed and wronged' is discussed. It is attributed to different narrators in parts. The commentary clarifies that 'acceptance' (qabul) in the hadith about one wash means permissibility/validity, not acceptance in the sight of Allah, which has additional conditions. The disagreement on interpreting 'addition' is summarized: some say it is adding beyond the prescribed number (three), but this is rejected because the Prophet encouraged lengthening the blaze (ghurrah) which is done by washing beyond the three times? Actually, the text says the opposite: lengthening the blaze is by adding beyond the limit, which seems contradictory. The correct opinion, according to al-Bada'i' and al-Hidayah, is that the threat applies to belief, not the act. Thus, one may wash more than three times for tranquility of heart without sin, as long as one does not believe it is obligatory. The passage then digresses into a discussion about repeating wudu in one sitting, intention (niyyah), and other details. The author addresses an apparent contradiction: some texts say repeating wudu in one sitting is disliked due to wasting water, while others say it is permissible if one intends a new wudu after finishing the first. He reconciles by noting different scenarios: the disliked repetition is when one repeats multiple times in one sitting aimlessly, while doing it once after finishing is not disliked, especially if motivated by a separate intention. The final part discusses the ruling on wiping (mash) three times: it is not sunnah and there is difference on whether it is disliked. The author inclines to no dislike. The passage ends with commentary on the intention for wudu, stating that the intention of the one performing wudu is to lift the state of ritual impurity or to perform prayer. This is the author's meaning, and it is derived from al-Kafi, so there is no need for the elaboration of al-Zayla'i. The passage closes with fragmentary text on imamate and the nature of sunnah mu'akkadah, comparing it to obligatory.

Key Terms
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah mu'akkadah): A confirmed sunnah; an act that the Prophet consistently performed and recommended, but whose omission does not invalidate the act and does not incur sin in the preferred view, though it may be disliked if habitual.
تثليث الغسل (tathlith al-ghusl): Washing each limb three times in wudu. The text specifies that the sunnah is the repetition of complete washes (ghaslat mustaw'ibat), not just handfuls of water.
غسلات مستوعبات (ghaslat mustaw'ibat): Complete washes that cover the entire limb. The repetition is of the complete wash, not just of scooping water without covering the limb.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi view, if a person washes each limb only once in wudu, which of the following is true?
A) His wudu is invalid and he must repeat it.
B) His wudu is valid but he has sinned by abandoning the sunnah.
C) His wudu is valid and he has not sinned, but he missed the reward of the sunnah.
D) His wudu is valid, but he must compensate by doing sajdah al-sahw.

Key Takeaway
Washing three times in wudu is a confirmed sunnah; one wash fulfills the obligation, and leaving the extra washes is not sinful, though it is better to follow the Prophet's practice.

Taharah — Purification

The Valid Intention for Wudu – Parsing the Ruling and Definition
Parsing the intention rule for wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the intention required for wudu and explain why a general intention of 'tahara' is insufficient.

Core Idea
Intending 'wudu' suffices for valid wudu; a general intention of 'purification' does not.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, the commentator parses the phrase 'wa niyyatuhu' from Kanz al-Daqa'iq. He clarifies what intention the person performing wudu must have, addressing potential confusion about whether a general intention of purification (tahara) is enough. The text also delves into the lexical and technical definition of niyyah itself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parsed phrase
The commentator explains 'wa niyyatuhu' from the matn. What does 'and his intention' refer to? It means the intention of the one performing wudu is removal of hadath or establishment of prayer.
This is the author's intended meaning per al-Kafi.
2
Analyze why 'tahara' is insufficient
The text argues that intending 'tahara' (purification) is not enough because tahara can mean removal of hadath or removal of najasa. Since wudu only removes minor hadath, a general intention of tahara is too broad.
Only intending 'wudu' or specific removal of hadath suffices.
3
List valid intentions
The commentator states that valid intentions include: removal of hadath, performing a specific prayer, making prayer permissible, or obeying the command (though the last is problematic before prayer time).
Intending 'wudu' is considered equivalent to removal of hadath.
4
Parse the definition of niyyah
The text defines niyyah linguistically (resolve of the heart) and terminologically (intending obedience to Allah). It addresses an objection that this definition does not cover prohibitions.
The preferred usul view reconciles this by considering restraint as an action.
5
Derive the Hanafi ruling
Synthesize: For valid wudu, the intention must be specific to wudu or its purpose (prayer). A general intention of 'tahara' does not count. The intention is a wajib condition, not a fard pillar.
This is based on the Hanafi distinction between fard and wajib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (ونيته) أي ونية المتوضىء رفع الحدث أو إقامة الصلاة هذا هو مراد المصنف كما عنه في الكافي فلا حاجة حينئذ إلى ما ذكره الزيلعي كما لا يخفى. واستفيد منه أن نية الطهارة لا تكفي في تحصيل السنة كأنه والله أعمل لأنها متنوّعة إلى إزالة الحدث أو الخبث فلم ينو خصوص الطهارة الصغرى. فعلى هذا لو نوى الوضوء فإنه يكون محصلاً لها لأن الوضوء الحدث سواء، لأن حقيقة الوضوء رفع الحدث كما حققناه أولاً. وعلى هذا فيصبح عود الضمير إلى الوضوء وسقط به كلام الزيلعي أيضاً كما لا يخفى مع أن الوضوء أخص من رفع الحدث لأنه يشمل الغسل، فعلى هذا نية الوضوء أولى قالوا المعتبر قصد رفع الحدث أو إقامة الصلاة كما ذكر أو استباحتها أو امتثال الأمر كما في المعراج، ولا يتأتي الأخير قبل دخول الوقت إذ ليس مأموراً به إلا أن يقال إن الوضوء لا يكون نفلاً لأنه شرط للصلاة وشرطها فرض ولا يخفى ما فيه. وهي لغة عزم القلب على الشيء، واصطلاحاً كما في التلويح قصد الطاعة والتقرب إلى الله تعالى في إيجاد الفعل واعترض عليه بأن هذا إنما يستقيم في العبادات المترتب عليها الثواب دون المنهيات المترتب عليها العقاب، فالصواب أن تفسر النية بتوجه القلب نحو إيجاد الفعل وتركه موافقاً لغرض من جلب نفع أو دفع ضر حالاً أو مالاً اهـ. وقد يقال : إن هذا الاعتراض مبني على أن المكلف به في النهي ليس هو الكف الذي هو الانتهاء وهو قول البعض والراجح في الأصول أنه لا تكليف إلا بفعل فهو في النهي كفه النفس فحينئذ دخل في إيجاد الفعل. وفي الصحاح العزم إرادة الفعل والقطع عليه والقصد إتيان الشيء. وذكر اليمني في شرح الشهاب ثم النية معنى وراء العلم فهي نوع إرادة كالقصد والعزيمة والهم والحب والودّ فالكل اسم للإرادة الحادثة لكن العزم اسم
His saying (and his intention): that is, the intention of the one performing wudu is the removal of hadath or the establishment of prayer. This is what the author intended, as [stated] in al-Kafi. Thus there is no need for what al-Zayla'i mentioned, as is not hidden. And from it is derived that the intention of purification (tahara) is not sufficient to achieve the sunna, because it is diversified into removal of hadath or removal of najasa, so he did not intend specifically minor purification. Accordingly, if he intends wudu, then he achieves it, because wudu and removal of hadath are the same, since the reality of wudu is removal of hadath as we verified earlier. And on this, the pronoun refers to wudu, and the statement of al-Zayla'i falls, as is not hidden, even though wudu is more specific than removal of hadath because it includes ghusl. So on this, intention of wudu is better. They said: the considered [view] is intending removal of hadath or establishment of prayer as mentioned, or making it permissible, or obeying the command as in al-Mi'raj, and the last is not feasible before the time enters since he is not commanded except that it be said that wudu is not supererogatory because it is a condition for prayer and its condition is obligatory, and what is in it is not hidden. It is linguistically the resolve of the heart upon something, and terminologically as in al-Talwih: intending obedience and drawing near to Allah the Exalted in performing the action. And it was objected that this is only correct for acts of worship upon which reward is attached, not for prohibitions upon which punishment is attached. So the correct is that niyyah is interpreted as the heart's direction toward performing or abandoning an action in accordance with a purpose of bringing benefit or repelling harm in [this] state or wealth. It may be said that this objection is based on the view that what is required in a prohibition is not the restraint which is desisting, which is the view of some, and the preferred [view] in usul is that there is no obligation except by action, so in a prohibition it is restraining the self; then it falls under performing an action. And in al-Sihah: al-'azm is the will to act and decisiveness, and al-qasd is coming to the thing. And al-Yamani mentioned in Sharh al-Shihab: then niyyah is a meaning beyond knowledge, so it is a type of will like intention, determination, resolve, love, and affection; all are names for the originated will, but al-'azm is a name.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, parsing the phrase 'wa niyyatuhu' (and his intention). The author begins by explaining that the intended meaning of the matn is that the person performing wudu must intend either the removal of hadath (ritual impurity) or the establishment of prayer. This is the author's (al-Nasafi's) goal, as confirmed in al-Kafi. Therefore, the objection raised by al-Zayla'i is unnecessary. The passage then discusses whether a general intention of 'tahara' (purification) suffices. It concludes that a general intention of 'tahara' is insufficient because tahara includes both removal of hadath (minor/major) and removal of najasa (filth). However, if one intends 'wudu' specifically, that is sufficient because wudu is synonymous with removing minor hadath. In fact, intending 'wudu' is even better because it is more specific. The text then lists the considered views on what intention is sufficient: intending removal of hadath, or intending prayer (i.e., performing a specific prayer), or intending making prayer permissible, or obeying the command. The last view is problematic before prayer time enters because the command is not yet addressed. The passage then provides linguistic and terminological definitions of niyyah (intention), citing various sources, and addresses an objection regarding its applicability to prohibitions. The final part discusses the lexical nuances of related terms like 'azm and qasd.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): Linguistically: resolve of the heart. Terminologically: intending obedience and closeness to Allah in performing an action; or directing the heart toward performing or abandoning an action for a worldly or otherworldly purpose.
رفع الحدث (raf' al-hadath): Removal of ritual impurity (either major or minor, but in context of wudu, minor impurity).
إقامة الصلاة (iqamat al-salah): Establishing prayer, i.e., performing the obligatory prayer; meant here as the intention to pray a specific prayer after wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following intentions is NOT sufficient for a valid wudu?
A) Intending to remove hadath
B) Intending to perform Dhuhr prayer
C) Intending to purify oneself (tahara)
D) Intending wudu

Key Takeaway
For valid wudu, the intention must be specific to wudu or its purpose; a general intention of purification is insufficient.

Definition of Niyyah and Its Distinction from 'Azm and Qasd
Defines Niyyah and distinguishes it from related terms

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish niyyah from 'azm and qasd and explain why niyyah includes both will and knowledge.

Core Idea
Niyyah is the heart's concurrent orientation with action, combining will and knowledge of the intended.

In Hanafi fiqh, niyyah (intention) is a foundational concept, especially for acts of worship. But what exactly is niyyah? This lesson unpacks its linguistic and technical definitions, clarifies an important objection, and distinguishes it from similar terms like 'azm (determination) and qasd (intention). Understanding these nuances ensures you correctly apply the concept in rulings.

Guided Path
1
1. Identify the linguistic and terminological definitions
Read the opening lines: niyyah linguistically is 'determination of the heart' and terminologically, as in al-Talwih, 'intending obedience and seeking nearness to Allah in performing the action'. Note that the terminological definition is limited to acts of worship.
The linguistic definition is broader.
2
2. Understand the objection and its resolution
An objection is raised: the terminological definition only covers acts of worship (reward), not prohibitions (punishment). The author then offers a corrected definition: 'orientation of the heart towards performing or abandoning an action, in accordance with a purpose of benefit or harm'. Also note the counter-argument based on usul: even prohibitions involve an action (restraining oneself).
The correction makes niyyah applicable to all actions.
3
3. Distinguish between 'azm, qasd, niyyah
From the lexicon and al-Yamani's commentary: 'azm is the will preceding the action, qasd is the will concurrent with the action, and niyyah is concurrent plus knowledge of the intended. All are types of created will, but niyyah includes an epistemic element.
Niyyah is the most specific.
4
4. Recognize that niyyah includes knowledge
The passage argues that an action cannot exist without will, e.g., standing, bowing, prostrating. Even a coerced person has will, though defective. Niyyah goes further: it requires knowledge of what one intends (e.g., which prayer).
This distinguishes niyyah from mere qasd.
5
5. Apply the definition with an example
Consider the phrase 'he intended fasting at night'. Here niyyah is used in the sense of 'azm (determination) because the fasting intention can be made before the day. But in the prayer, niyyah must be concurrent with the takbir.
Context determines the precise meaning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهي لغة عزم القلب على الشيء، واصطلاحاً كما في التلويح قصد الطاعة والتقرب إلى الله تعالى في إيجاد الفعل واعترض عليه بأن هذا إنما يستقيم في العبادات المترتب عليها الثواب دون المنهيات المترتب عليها العقاب، فالصواب أن تفسر النية بتوجه القلب نحو إيجاد الفعل وتركه موافقاً لغرض من جلب نفع أو دفع ضر حالاً أو مالاً اهـ. وقد يقال : إن هذا الاعتراض مبني على أن المكلف به في النهي ليس هو الكف الذي هو الانتهاء وهو قول البعض والراجح في الأصول أنه لا تكليف إلا بفعل فهو في النهي كفه النفس فحينئذ دخل في إيجاد الفعل. وفي الصحاح العزم إرادة الفعل والقطع عليه والقصد إتيان الشيء. وذكر اليمني في شرح الشهاب ثم النية معنى وراء العلم فهي نوع إرادة كالقصد والعزيمة والهم والحب والودّ فالكل اسم للإرادة الحادثة لكن العزم اسم للمتقدم على الفعل والقصد اسم للمقترن بالفعل والنية اسم للمقترن بالفعل مع دخوله تحت العلم بالمنوي، وهذا لأن الفعل لا يوجد بدون الإرادة فإذا قام الرجل من قعوده لا بد وأن يكون مريداً للقيام وإن لم تعمل إرادته القيام وقد يركع الرجل ويسجد ذاهلاً عن معرفة إرادة الركوع والسجود ويستحيل وجودهما بدون الإرادة بالكلية لأن الإرادة صنو القدرة وإنما المفقود العلم لا غير ولذا قلنا للمكره إرادة. وإن كانت فاسدة بمقابلة إرادة المكره لكن قد تذكر النية مقام العزيمة كما في قولنا ونوى الصوم بالليل أي عزم عليه وأطال فيه فليراجع لاشتماله على فوائد كثيرة.
And it [niyyah] linguistically is the determination of the heart upon a thing. Terminologically, as in al-Talwih: intending obedience and seeking nearness to Allah Almighty in performing the action. An objection was raised that this only applies to acts of worship that entail reward, not prohibited acts that entail punishment. The correct view is to interpret niyyah as the heart's orientation towards performing or abandoning an action, in accordance with a purpose of attaining benefit or repelling harm, present or future, etc. It may be said that this objection is based on the view that the obligated matter in a prohibition is not the restraint which is desisting—that is the opinion of some; but the preponderant view in usul is that there is no obligation except an action, so in the case of a prohibition, it is restraining oneself, thus it falls under performing an action. In al-Sihah: determination is the will to act and the resolution upon it; intention is the undertaking of a thing. Al-Yamani mentioned in Sharh al-Shihab that niyyah is a meaning beyond knowledge; it is a type of will, like intention, determination, resolve, love, and affection—all are names for the created will, but determination is a name for [the will] preceding the action, intention is a name for that concurrent with the action, and niyyah is a name for that concurrent with the action while entering under knowledge of the intended. This is because an action does not exist without will; if a man stands from his sitting, he must be willing to stand even if his will does not effect the standing. A man may bow and prostrate while heedless of recognizing the will to bow and prostrate, yet it is impossible for them to exist without will entirely, because will is the counterpart of capability; only knowledge is lacking. That is why we say that the coerced person has will, even if it is defective compared to the will of the one coercing. However, niyyah is sometimes used in place of determination, as in our saying: 'And he intended fasting at night,' meaning he determined upon it. He went on at length, so let it be referred to for its many benefits.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage is a definition and terminological delineation of Niyyah (intention) in the Hanafi school. It begins with the linguistic meaning: determination of the heart. The terminological definition from al-Talwih is given as intending obedience and seeking nearness to Allah in performing an action. An objection is raised: this definition only fits acts of worship (which bring reward), not prohibitions (which bring punishment). The correct definition offered is that Niyyah is orientation of the heart towards performing or abandoning an action in accordance with a purpose (benefit or harm). The author then notes that the objection can be countered because even in prohibitions the obligated action is 'restraining oneself', which is a voluntary act. The passage further distinguishes between related terms: 'azm (determination), qasd (intention), and niyyah, citing lexicons and the explanation of al-Yamani. Niyyah is specifically the will concurrent with action and accompanied by knowledge of the intended. The argument that actions cannot exist without will is supported by examples: standing, bowing, prostrating. Even a coerced person has will, though defective. Finally, niyyah can sometimes mean 'azm (determination), as in the phrase 'he intended fasting at night'.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): Linguistically: determination of the heart. Terminologically: orientation of the heart towards performing or abandoning an action, concurrent with the action and accompanied by knowledge of the intended.
عزم (azm): Determination: the will to act preceding the action.
قصد (qasd): Intention: the will concurrent with the action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Niyyah precedes the action while qasd is concurrent.
B) Niyyah includes knowledge of the intended act, while qasd does not.
C) Niyyah is only for acts of worship, while qasd is for worldly matters.
D) Niyyah is a type of 'azm.

Key Takeaway
Niyyah is a specific type of will that is concurrent with the action and includes knowledge of the intended act, distinguishing it from 'azm (preceding will) and qasd (concurrent will without knowledge).

Niyyah in Wudu: Default Sunnah, Exceptional Condition
States default sunnah ruling and exceptional condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the default ruling of niyyah in wudu according to the Hanafi school and identify the two exceptional cases where niyyah becomes a condition.

Core Idea
In the Hanafi school, niyyah in wudu is generally a confirmed sunnah, but it is a condition when using donkey leftover water or date drink.

Many assume that intention (niyyah) is always obligatory in wudu, but the Hanafi school differentiates. This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies that the default ruling is sunnah mu'akkadah—a strongly recommended but not obligatory act. However, there are two specific types of water (su'r al-himar and nabidh al-tamr) where niyyah becomes a binding condition for the validity of wudu as a key to prayer. This nuanced ruling reflects the Hanafi approach to usul and practical fiqh.

Guided Path
1
State the default ruling
Read the first sentence: niyyah in wudu (except the two cases) is a confirmed sunnah, not a condition. Understand that 'confirmed sunnah' means it is highly recommended but not obligatory; wudu is valid without it, though reward is diminished.
Note the phrase 'على الصحيح' (according to the correct view) indicating this is the mufta bihi position.
2
Identify the exception
Locate the phrase 'غير التوضؤ بسؤر الحمار وبنبيذ التمر' – except for wudu with donkey leftover water or date drink. Recognize that these are the two specific cases where the ruling changes.
These waters are considered pure but are borderline; hence the extra precaution requires niyyah.
3
Understand the condition's scope
The text says niyyah is a condition 'في كون الوضوء مفتاحاً للصلاة' (for wudu being a key to prayer). This means without niyyah, wudu with these waters does not fulfill the required purification for prayer. However, the next sentence clarifies that niyyah is also a condition for reward according to the majority view.
There is a minority view that one can still get reward without niyyah, but the relied-upon position is that reward requires intention.
4
Note the details of niyyah
The passage specifies that the time for niyyah is at the beginning of washing the face, the place is the heart, and verbalizing it is recommended. This applies to all cases, but the condition status only changes in the two exceptional cases.
Verbalization is mustahab, not required; the heart intention suffices.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اعلم أن النية في غير التوضؤ بسؤر الحمار وبنبيذ التمر سنة مؤكدة على الصحيح وليست بشرط في كون الوضوء مفتاحاً للصلاة. ووقتها عند غسل الوجه ومحلها القلب والتلفظ بها مستحب كذا في السراج الوهاج. وأما النية في التوضؤ بسؤر الحمار أو بنبيذ التمر فشرط كذا في شرح الجمع والنقاية معزيين إلى الكفاية قيدنا بقولنا في كونه مفتاحاً لأنها شرط في كونه سبباً للثواب على الأصح، وقيل يثاب بغير نية.
Then know that niyyah, except in the case of performing wudu with the leftover water of a donkey or with date drink, is a confirmed sunnah according to the correct view, and it is not a condition for wudu being a key to prayer. Its time is at washing the face, its place is the heart, and verbalizing it is recommended, as stated in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. As for niyyah in performing wudu with the leftover water of a donkey or with date drink, it is a condition, as stated in Sharh al-Jama‘ and al-Nuqayah, attributed to al-Kifayah. We qualified by our saying 'for it being a key' because it is a condition for it being a cause of reward according to the most correct view, and it is said that one receives reward without niyyah.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on the role of intention (niyyah) in wudu (ablution). The default ruling is that niyyah is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah), not a condition (shart) for the validity of wudu as a key to prayer. The time for niyyah is at the start of washing the face, the place is the heart, and it is recommended to utter it verbally. However, there is an exception: when performing wudu with the leftover water (su'r) of a donkey or with nabidh al-tamr (date drink), niyyah becomes a condition. The author qualifies that it is a condition specifically for the wudu being a key to prayer—i.e., for its validity as purification. However, even there, niyyah is a condition for earning reward (thawab) according to the most correct view, with an alternative opinion that reward is attained even without niyyah.

Key Terms
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah mu'akkadah): A confirmed sunnah: a recommended act that the Prophet consistently performed, omission of which is disliked but not sinful.
سؤر الحمار (su'r al-himar): The leftover water (remnant) from a donkey's drinking; its purity is disputed, and wudu with it requires niyyah.
نبيذ التمر (nabidh al-tamr): Date drink; a liquid made by soaking dates in water. Used for wudu in absence of water, but only with certain conditions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, in which case is niyyah a condition (shart) in wudu?
A) When performing wudu with pure water.
B) When using leftover water of a donkey or date drink.
C) When wudu is performed before the prayer time.
D) When one intends to earn reward.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, niyyah in wudu is a confirmed sunnah except when using the leftover water of a donkey or date drink, where it becomes a condition for validity.
