Hanafi Response to Shafi'i Proof on Niyyah in Wudu
Refutes the Shafi'i argument that the hadith 'إنما الأعمال بالنية' makes niyyah a condition for wudu validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi refutation of the Shafi'i argument that niyyah is a condition for wudu validity based on the hadith 'innama al-a'mal bi al-niyyah'.

Core Idea
The hadith governs otherworldly reward, not worldly validity—wudu without niyyah is valid.

This lesson examines a classic dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the role of intention (niyyah) in the validity of wudu. The Shafi'i school relies on the famous hadith 'إنما الأعمال بالنية' (Actions are but by intentions) to argue that intention is a condition for wudu. The Hanafi school, however, offers a sophisticated usul-based interpretation, distinguishing between the worldly and otherworldly dimensions of the ruling. By the end, you will understand the methodological underpinnings of the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
State the Shafi'i position and its proof
Identify that al-Shafi'i argues niyyah is a condition for wudu based on the hadith. He interprets 'actions' as acts of worship and uses qiyas to tayammum.
2
Identify the Hanafi response
The Hanafi usulis argue that the literal meaning of the hadith is abandoned because it leads to impossibility (many acts exist without intention). Thus, it is metaphorical (majaz).
3
Analyze the concept of metaphorical interpretation
The implied meaning is 'the judgment (hukm) of actions depends on intentions.' The term 'hukm' is then ambiguous (mushtarak) between worldly and otherworldly judgments.
In Hanafi usul, a mushtarak term carries no generality ('umum).
4
Determine the agreed-upon meaning
The Hanafis argue that the only agreed-upon meaning between them and al-Shafi'i is the otherworldly judgment (reward/punishment), since both schools agree reward depends on intention. The worldly validity is not proven by this hadith.
5
Identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Hanafi: wudu without niyyah is valid but reward is lacking. Shafi'i: wudu without niyyah is invalid (batil). This difference affects fatwa and practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم استدل الشافعي على اشتراطها فيه بالحديث المشهور المتفق على صحته إنما الأعمال بالنية ووجهه أن المراد بالأعمال العبادات لأن كثيراً من الأعمال تعتبر شرعاً بلا نية فيكون المراد إنما صحة العبادات بالنية والوضوء عبادة لأنها فعل ما يرضي الرب وهو كذلك فصار كالتيمم. ولنا على ما ذكره الأصوليون أن حقيقة هذا التركيب متروكة بدلالة محل الكلام لأن كلمة «إنما للحصر وقد دخلت على المعرف بلام الاستغراق، وذلك يقتضي أن لا يوجد عمل بلا نية ولا يمكن حمله على العموم لأن كثيراً من الأعمال يوجد بلا نية فصار مجازاً . عن حكمه، فالتقدير حكم الأعمال بالنيات من إطلاق اسم السبب على المسبب، حذف المضاف وإقامة المضاف إليه مقامه. والحكم نوعان مختلفان أحدهما أخروي وهو الثواب والإثم وهو بناء على صدق العزيمة وعدمه، والثاني دنيوي وهو الجواز والفساد وهو بناء على وجود الأركان والشرائط وعدمها، ولما اختلف الحكمان صار الاسم بعد كونه مجازاً مشتركاً. ويكفي في تصحيحه ما هو المتفق عليه وهو الحكم الأخروي ولا دليل على ما اختلف فيه فلا يصلح تقديره حجة علينا فاندفع بهذا التقرير ما أورده في الكشف وشرح المغني وشرح المنار من أن قولهم أن الحكم مشترك ولا عموم له ممنوع بل هذا في المشترك أو من لمنافاته لما مر من أنه يكون واجباً ومندوباً قوله : (صار الاسم بعد كونه مجازاً مشتركاً) لأن التقدير حكم الأعمال وهذا مجاز كما تقدم تقريره والحكم المقدر مشترك بين النوعين المختلفين فنريد منهما ما هو المتفق عليه عندنا وعند الشافعي رحمه الله تعالى وهو الحكم الأخروي إذ لا ثواب بدون النية اتفاقاً، وأما الدنيوي فلا دليل عليه قوله : (فاندفع بهذا التقرير ما أورده في الكشف الخ) اعلم أن الأصوليين قالوا: لما صار الاسم مشتركاً والمشترك لا عموم له عندنا أردنا المعنى المتفق عليه الذي هو الأخروي، وأورد عليهم أن الذي لا عموم له هو المشترك اللفظي ولا نسلم أن الحكم مشترك بين
Then al-Shafi‘i argued for its conditionality [of niyyah in wudu] with the well-known hadith, whose authenticity is agreed upon: 'Actions are but by intentions.' His reasoning is that the intended meaning of 'actions' is acts of worship, because many actions are considered legally without intention, so the meaning is: 'The validity of acts of worship is by intention.' And wudu is an act of worship because it is doing what pleases the Lord, and so it is like tayammum. Our position, as stated by the usulis, is that the literal meaning of this construction is abandoned due to the context of the discourse, because the word 'innama' indicates restriction and it has entered upon a definite noun with the lam of generality, which implies that no action exists without intention. But it cannot be taken generally because many actions exist without intention, so it becomes metaphorical regarding its ruling. Thus the implied meaning is: 'The judgment of actions depends on intentions'—by synecdoche (ism al-sabab ‘ala al-musabbab), with the deletion of the genitive and substitution of the noun. The judgment is of two different types: one is otherworldly, namely reward and punishment, which depends on the sincerity of resolve or its absence; the second is worldly, namely validity and invalidity, which depends on the existence of pillars and conditions or their absence. Since the two judgments differ, the noun becomes, after being metaphorical, ambiguous (mushtarak). It suffices for its correction what is agreed upon, which is the otherworldly judgment, and there is no evidence for the disputed one, so it cannot be used as proof against us. Thus, by this exposition, what was mentioned in al-Kashf, Sharh al-Mughni, and Sharh al-Manar is refuted: that their saying that the judgment is common and has no generality is denied; rather, this applies to the common [term] or from what contradicts what has passed that it is obligatory and recommended. His saying: ('The noun becomes, after being metaphorical, ambiguous') because the implied is 'the judgment of actions' and this is metaphorical as previously explained, and the implied judgment is common between the two different types. We intend from them what is agreed upon by us and al-Shafi‘i, may Allah have mercy on him, which is the otherworldly judgment, since there is no reward without intention by consensus. As for the worldly, there is no evidence for it. His saying: ('Thus, by this exposition, what was mentioned in al-Kashf is refuted…') Know that the usulis said: When the noun became ambiguous, and the ambiguous has no generality in our view, we intended the agreed-upon meaning, which is the otherworldly. An objection was raised against them that that which has no generality is the lexically ambiguous term (mushtarak lafzi), and we do not concede that the judgment is ambiguous between...
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage presents a formal inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi‘i on the requirement of niyyah (intention) in wudu. The Shafi‘i argument relies on the famous hadith 'إنما الأعمال بالنية' (Actions are but by intentions). He interprets 'actions' as acts of worship, so the hadith means that the validity (sihhah) of worship depends on intention. Since wudu is an act of worship, it requires intention, analogous to tayammum. The Hanafi response, given by the usulis (principles scholars), is a nuanced analysis of the hadith. First, the literal meaning (haqiqah) of the construction is abandoned because the context (muhawarah/mawqif) indicates that the hadith cannot be taken universally (many actions exist without intention). Thus it is metaphorical (majaz). The implied meaning is: 'The judgment (hukm) of actions depends on intentions' — the noun 'judgment' is deleted, and the cause (intention) is used for the effect (judgment). Then, judgment is of two kinds: otherworldly (reward/punishment) and worldly (validity/invalidity). After metaphor, the term 'hukm' becomes ambiguous (mushtarak) between these two. The Hanafi school takes the agreed-upon meaning (otherworldly) because there is consensus that reward depends on intention. The worldly judgment (validity/invalidity) is not proven by this hadith, so it cannot be used against the Hanafi view that niyyah is not a condition for the validity of wudu. The author notes that this refutation addresses objections in works like al-Kashf, Sharh al-Mughni, and Sharh al-Manar. The passage ends with a discussion of the usuli principle that a mushtarak term lacks generality ('umum); the Hanafis apply this to argue that the hadith does not give a general ruling covering both worldly and otherworldly judgments.

Key Terms
إنما الأعمال بالنية (innama al-a'mal bi al-niyyah): The hadith meaning 'Actions are but by intentions.' Used by Shafi'i to argue that intention is required for validity of worship.
مجاز (majaz): Metaphorical usage: the hadith cannot be taken literally, so it is interpreted metaphorically.
مشترك (mushtarak): Ambiguous term: 'hukm' (judgment) becomes ambiguous between otherworldly and worldly meanings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response, what type of judgment does 'إنما الأعمال بالنية' refer to?
A) The worldly validity (sihhah) of acts.
B) The otherworldly reward and punishment.
C) Both worldly and otherworldly equally.
D) Only the intention of the heart.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school interprets the hadith 'إنما الأعمال بالنية' as referring to otherworldly judgment, not the worldly validity of acts like wudu.

6 min
Ruling on Niyyah in Wudu: General Principle and Exceptions
Defines niyyah and states its ruling with exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on niyyah in wudu and identify the two exceptional cases where it becomes a condition (shart) for validity.

Core Idea
Niyyah in wudu is generally a stressed sunnah, but it is a condition for validity when using donkeys' leftover water or date drink.

This passage from the Book of Purification clarifies the precise status of niyyah (intention) in wudu. The Hanafi school distinguishes between the general case, where niyyah is recommended but not required, and two exceptional cases where it is obligatory for the wudu to be valid. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying the rules of purification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is wudu. The general ruling on niyyah in wudu is that it is a stressed sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah).
The text explicitly states: 'النِّيَّةُ فِي غَيْرِ التَّوَضُّؤِ بِسُؤْرِ الْحِمَارِ وَبِنَبِيذِ التَّمْرِ سُنَّةٌ مُؤَكَّدَةٌ عَلَى الصَّحِيحِ'
2
Distinguish between iradah and niyyah
The author defines niyyah as intention connected to the action with knowledge of the intended act. This distinguishes it from mere will (iradah), which is always present in any voluntary action.
Example: a person bowing absentmindedly still has will (iradah) but lacks knowledge of the specific act, so niyyah is absent.
3
Locate the general rule
Niyyah in wudu with ordinary water is a stressed sunnah, not a condition for validity. It is recommended but not required.
The text says 'وَلَيْسَتْ بِشَرْطٍ فِي كَوْنِ الْوُضُوءِ مِفْتَاحًا لِلصَّلَاةِ' (it is not a condition for wudu to be a key to prayer).
4
Identify the exceptions
In two specific cases, niyyah becomes a condition (shart) for the validity of wudu: (1) when using the leftover water of a donkey (su'r al-himar), and (2) when using date drink (nabidh al-tamr).
The text states: 'وَأَمَّا النِّيَّةُ فِي التَّوَضُّؤِ بِسُؤْرِ الْحِمَارِ أَوْ بِنَبِيذِ التَّمْرِ فَشَرْطٌ'
5
Note the time, place, and verbalization
The time for niyyah is at washing the face; its place is the heart; and verbalizing it is recommended (mustahabb).
These details are given in the text: 'وَوَقْتُهَا عِنْدَ غَسْلِ الْوَجْهِ وَمَحَلُّهَا الْقَلْبُ وَالتَّلَفُّظُ بِهَا مُسْتَحَبٌّ'

Source Text

كتاب الطهارة
للمتقدم على الفعل والقصد اسم للمقترن بالفعل والنية اسم للمقترن بالفعل مع دخوله تحت العلم بالمنوي، وهذا لأن الفعل لا يوجد بدون الإرادة فإذا قام الرجل من قعوده لا بد وأن يكون مريداً للقيام وإن لم تعمل إرادته القيام وقد يركع الرجل ويسجد . ذاهلاً عن معرفة إرادة الركوع والسجود ويستحيل وجودهما بدون الإرادة بالكلية لأن الإرادة صنو القدرة وإنما المفقود العلم لا غير ولذا قلنا للمكره إرادة. وإن كانت فاسدة بمقابلة إرادة المكره لكن قد تذكر النية مقام العزيمة كما في قولنا ونوى الصوم بالليل أي عزم عليه وأطال فيه فليراجع لاشتماله على فوائد كثيرة. ثم اعلم أن النية في غير التوضؤ بسؤر الحمار وبنبيذ التمر سنة مؤكدة على الصحيح وليست بشرط في كون الوضوء مفتاحاً للصلاة. ووقتها عند غسل الوجه ومحلها القلب والتلفظ بها مستحب كذا في السراج الوهاج.
وأما النية في التوضؤ بسؤر الحمار أو بنبيذ التمر فشرط كذا في شرح الجمع والنقاية معزيين إلى الكفاية
Book of Purification. For the one preceding, action and intention are names for what is connected to the action, and niyyah is a name for what is connected to the action with its inclusion under knowledge of the intended. This is because action does not exist without will; when a man stands from his sitting, he must be intending to stand even if his will does not effect the standing. A man may bow and prostrate while oblivious to knowing the intention of bowing and prostration, but their existence without any will is impossible because will is the counterpart of ability; only knowledge is lacking. For this reason we say that the coerced person has will, even if it is defective in comparison to the will of the coercer. But niyyah may be mentioned in place of determination, as in our saying 'he intended fasting at night', i.e., he resolved upon it. He elaborated at length; let one refer back for it contains many benefits. Then know that niyyah in wudu other than with the leftover water of a donkey or with date drink is a stressed sunnah according to the correct view, and it is not a condition for wudu to be a key to prayer. Its time is at washing the face, its place is the heart, and verbalization is recommended. Thus in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. As for niyyah in wudu with the leftover water of a donkey or with date drink, it is a condition. Thus in Sharh al-Jam' wa al-Niqayah, attributed to al-Kifayah.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the book of purification. It begins by defining niyyah and distinguishing it from iradah (will) and qasd (intention). The author explains that every action requires a will, but niyyah specifically involves knowledge of the intended act. He then states the general ruling: niyyah in wudu is a stressed sunnah (sunnah mu'akkada), meaning it is recommended but not required for validity. However, there is an exception: when performing wudu with the leftover water of a donkey (su'r al-himar) or with date drink (nabidh al-tamr), niyyah becomes a condition (shart) for the validity of wudu as a key to prayer. The timing of niyyah is when washing the face, its place is the heart, and verbalizing it is mustahabb. This ruling is based on the correct view in the Hanafi school, as referenced from authoritative works.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): Intention connected to the action with knowledge of the intended act.
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah mu'akkadah): A stressed recommended act; omission is disliked but does not invalidate the act.
شرط (shart): A condition without which the act is invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, in which of the following cases does the Hanafi school consider niyyah a condition (shart) for the validity of wudu?
A) Wudu with ordinary water.
B) Wudu with the leftover water of a donkey (su'r al-himar).
C) Wudu with rainwater.
D) Wudu with sea water.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, niyyah in wudu is a stressed sunnah except when using su'r al-himar or nabidh al-tamr, where it becomes a condition for validity.

12 min
Debate with al-Shafi'i on Niyyah in Wudu
Presents al-Shafi'i's proof from hadith and the Hanafi response regarding niyyah in wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi interpretation of the hadith 'innama al-a'mal bi'l-niyyah' and contrast it with the Shafi'i view, identifying the thamarah al-khilaf regarding wudu without niyyah.

Core Idea
The hadith refers to the Hereafter, not worldly validity — wudu without niyyah is valid but unrewarded.

In this lesson, we delve into the classical Hanafi-Shafi'i debate on whether intention (niyyah) is a condition for the validity of wudu. The Shafi'i school argues from the famous hadith 'innama al-a'mal bi'l-niyyah', while the Hanafi school offers a sophisticated linguistic and legal analysis to show that the hadith concerns reward, not validity. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to interpret texts and appreciate how different usul principles yield different fiqh rulings.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi school's ruling: niyyah is not a condition for the worldly validity of wudu (sihhah), but is required for otherworldly reward (thawab).
This is the core of the disagreement.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i holds niyyah to be a condition for the validity of wudu, citing the same hadith.
The evidence is common, but interpretation differs.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine al-Shafi'i's dalil: the hadith 'innama al-a'mal bi'l-niyyah' is taken as general (amm), indicating that all actions require niyyah for validity. Qiyas with tayammum is also used.
The qiyas argument is an additional support.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Understand the Hanafi rebuttal: the hadith cannot be taken literally because many actions are valid without niyyah. It is metaphorical (majaz), and the intended meaning is 'the ruling of actions is by intentions'. The term 'ruling' (hukm) is common between worldly and otherworldly aspects; the agreed-upon meaning is the otherworldly. The qiyas with tayammum is invalid because tayammum is a substitute (badal) requiring additional conditions.
This response relies on usul al-fiqh concepts of majaz, mushtarak, and qiyas rejection.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: a person who performs wudu without niyyah has a valid wudu according to Hanafis and may pray, but loses reward. According to Shafi'is, the wudu is invalid and prayer is not accepted.
This affects everyday practice for millions.

يعم
النوعين اشتراكاً لفظياً بأن يوضع بإزاء كل منهما وضعاً على حدة بل هو مشترك معنوي موضوع للأثر الثابت بالشيء فيعم الحكمين كما الحيوان الإنسان والفرس وغيرهما، واللون السواد والبياض ونحوهما فإرادة النوعين لا تكون من عموم المشترك في شيء فلا حاجة إلى إرادة أحدهما لتصحيحه، وأنت خبير بأن التقرير الذي قرره الشارح هو عين ما قرره الأصوليون فيرد عليه ما أورد عليهم، فكيف يندفع الإيراد بمجرد تقريره وليس فيه شيء زائد عليه يصلح للدفع اللهم إلا أن يقال : إن معنى تقريره أنا نريد بالحكم المعنى المتفق عليه وندع الآخر الذي لا دليل عليه، لا لما قالوا من عدم عموم المشترك بل استغناء من المعنيين بأحدهما المتفق عليه سواء كان الحكم مشتركاً لفظياً أو معنوياً. وبهذا يحصل الدفع للإيراد المذكور ولكن ينافي الحمل على هذا المعنى قوله ويكفي في تصحيحه فإنه ظاهر فيما قاله الأصوليون فليتأمل . قوله : (مع أن الإكمل في تقريره أجاب عنه) أي عن الإيراد المذكور وحاصله كما في شرح المنار للشارح أن المشترك المعنوي إن كان متواطئاً قبل العموم وإن كان مشككاً لا يقبله. قوله : (عليهما ) أي على الحكمين قوله : (لكن الثواب والعقاب ليسا كذلك على المذهب (الصحيح أي خلافاً للمعتزلة بل الأعمال عند أهل السنة علامات محضة عليهما كما تقرر في موضعه فإطلاق الحكم عليها يكون بالمعنى الآخر بالضرورة ولا معنى
We restricted [our statement] by saying 'in its being a key' because it is a condition for it to be a cause of reward according to the most correct view, and it was said one is rewarded without intention. Then al-Shafi'i argued for its conditionality [in wudu] by the famous hadith agreed upon as authentic: 'Actions are only by intentions.' His reasoning is that by 'actions' is meant acts of worship, because many actions are considered valid legally without intention, so the meaning is that the validity of acts of worship is by intention, and wudu is an act of worship because it is doing what pleases the Lord. And it is thus, so it becomes like tayammum. Our proof, according to what the usuliyyun have mentioned, is that the literal meaning of this construction is abandoned by evidence of the context, because the word 'innama' is for restriction and it has entered upon the definite noun with the generic lam, and that requires that no action exists without intention, and it cannot be taken as general because many actions exist without intention, so it becomes metaphorical regarding its ruling. The implied meaning is: 'the ruling of actions is by intentions' by way of using the name of the cause for the effect, omitting the annexed term and putting the annexed-to term in its place. And the ruling is of two different types: one otherworldly, which is reward and punishment, based on the truth of determination or its lack; and the second worldly, which is permissibility and invalidity, based on the existence of pillars and conditions or their absence. Since the two rulings differ, the word after being metaphorical becomes common (mushtarak). What suffices for its interpretation is what is agreed upon, which is the otherworldly ruling, and there is no evidence for what is disputed, so it is not valid to take it as a proof against us. By this exposition, what was objected in al-Kashf, Sharh al-Mughni, and Sharh al-Manar is repelled: that their statement that the ruling is common and has no generality is denied; rather this is in the verbal common term.... [The text continues with detailed discussion]
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the necessity of niyyah in wudu. The discussion begins with a qualification: the earlier ruling that niyyah is not a condition for the validity of wudu as a key to prayer is clarified; it is a condition for reward. Then al-Shafi'i's argument is presented: he uses the well-known hadith 'innama al-a'mal bi'l-niyyat' to prove that niyyah is required for the validity of wudu, as wudu is an act of worship. The Hanafi response is detailed: the hadith cannot be taken literally because many actions are valid without niyyah. The construction is metaphorical; the intended meaning is 'the ruling of actions is by intentions', and the word 'ruling' can refer to either the otherworldly (reward) or worldly (validity) aspect. The Hanafis argue that the agreed-upon meaning is the otherworldly one, as there is no proof for the worldly. They also address objections from later commentaries regarding the nature of the common term (mushtarak). The text further explores the difference between acts and omissions, concluding that the hadith covers both, but niyyah is required for reward in omissions as well, not for escaping prohibition. The passage critiques the Shafi'i distinction between wudu (requiring niyyah) and removing impurity (not requiring niyyah) as weak. Ultimately, the Hanafi position is that niyyah is not a condition for the worldly validity of wudu, only for reward.

Key Terms
إنما الأعمال بالنية (innama al-a'mal bi'l-niyyah): A hadith meaning 'Actions are only by intentions', used as the main proof by al-Shafi'i.
مجاز (majaz): Metaphorical usage; the hadith is taken metaphorically, not literally, because literal reading leads to contradiction with observable facts.
مشترك لفظي (mushtarak lafzi): A word that has multiple distinct meanings, but here the word 'hukm' is argued to be either literal or common between two meanings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi argument, what is the intended meaning of the word 'al-a'mal' (actions) in the hadith 'innama al-a'mal bi'l-niyyat'?
A) All actions, including sinful acts
B) Only acts of worship (ibadat)
C) The ruling of actions in the Hereafter, i.e., reward and punishment
D) The worldly validity of actions

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that niyyah in wudu is required for reward, not for validity, based on a metaphorical interpretation of the hadith 'innama al-a'mal bi'l-niyyah'.

The Necessity of Intention in Wudu: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute over necessity of niyyah in wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that intention (niyyah) is not required for the validity of wudu as a condition for prayer and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Intention is required for reward, not for validity: wudu without intention still makes prayer valid.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq tackles a classic dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: does wudu require intention (niyyah) to be valid? The commentator defends the Hanafi position that niyyah is not a condition for wudu's validity in making prayer permissible, though it is necessary for wudu to be an act of worship meriting reward. By examining the Prophet's teaching of wudu to a Bedouin and the nature of conditions in worship, the Hanafi school establishes a clear distinction. In this lesson, you will trace the arguments and evidence presented.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
Determine the exact legal question being disputed: whether intention (niyyah) is a condition for the validity of wudu as a prerequisite for prayer.
2
State the Hanafi position
Articulate the Hanafi view: niyyah is not a condition for wudu's validity; it only affects reward. Wudu performed without intention still fulfills the requirement for prayer.
The Hana is position is based on the Prophet's practice and the nature of conditions.
3
Identify the Shafi'i objection
State the Shafi'i argument: wudu is an act of worship (ibadah), and all acts of worship require intention for validity. They cite hadith 'al-tuhur shatr al-iman'.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Examine how the Hanafi commentator rebuts: the Prophet taught a Bedouin wudu without mentioning intention; conditions for prayer (like covering the nakedness) do not require intention; tayammum is distinguished because it is purely devotional.
The response uses the Bedouin hadith as key evidence and draws analogy with other conditions.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence: if wudu is done without intention, Hanafis consider the prayer valid (but wudu earns no reward); Shafi'is consider the prayer invalid.
This difference affects daily practice for millions of Muslims.

كتاب الطهارة
اللفظي ، أما المشترك المعنوي فله عموم كالشيء والحكم منه فيتناول الكل باعتبار المعنى الأعم إذ تفسير الحكم الأثر الثابت بالشيء .ا.هـ. مع أن الأكمل في تقريره أجاب عنه بأن هذا إنما يستقيم أن لو كان الحكم مقولاً عليهما بالتواطؤ وهو ممنوع، لأن الجواز والفساد وإن كانا أثرين ثابتين بالأعمال موجبين لها لكن الثواب والعقاب ليسا كذلك على المذهب الصحيح ا هـ. يعني لتخلفهما في الأول بعدم القبول الصحة، وفي الثاني بالعفو من الله تعالى . والمراد بالأعمال ما يشمل على القلب فيدخل فيه كف النفس بالنهي فإنه عمل، ولا ترد النية لأنها خارجة لمعنى يخصها وهو لزوم التسلسل لكن اعتبار النية للتروك إنما هو لحصول الثواب لا للخروج عن عهدة النهي، لأن مناط الوعيد بالعقاب في النهي هو فعل المنهي، فمجرد تركه كاف في انتفاء الوعيد ومناط الثواب في المنهي كف النفس عنه وهو عمل مندرج في الحديث وعلى هذا ففرق الشافعية بين الوضوء وإزالة النجاسة بأن الوضوء فعل فيفتقر إلى النية وطهارة النجاسة من باب التروك فلا تفتقر إلى النية كترك الزنا ضعيف، فإن التكليف أبداً لا يقع إلا بالفعل الذي هو مقدور المكلف لا بعدم الفعل الذي هو غير مقدور وجوده قبل التكليف كما عرف في مقتضى النهي أنه كف النفس عن الفعل لا عدم الفعل والترك ليس بفعل، ولهذا لا يثاب المكلف على التروك إلا إذا ترك قاصداً، فلا يثاب على ترك الزنا إلا إذا كف نفسه عند قصداً لا إذا اشتغل عنه بفعل آخر كالنوم والعبادة وتركه بلا قصد فلا فرق بين الفعل والترك الموجبين للثواب والعقاب .
يعم
النوعين اشتراكاً لفظياً بأن يوضع بإزاء كل منهما وضعاً على حدة بل هو مشترك معنوي موضوع للأثر الثابت بالشيء فيعم الحكمين كما الحيوان الإنسان والفرس وغيرهما، واللون السواد والبياض ونحوهما فإرادة النوعين لا تكون من عموم المشترك في شيء فلا حاجة إلى إرادة أحدهما لتصحيحه، وأنت خبير بأن التقرير الذي قرره الشارح هو عين ما قرره الأصوليون فيرد عليه ما أورد عليهم، فكيف يندفع الإيراد بمجرد تقريره وليس فيه شيء زائد عليه يصلح للدفع اللهم إلا أن يقال : إن معنى تقريره أنا نريد بالحكم المعنى المتفق عليه وندع الآخر الذي لا دليل عليه، لا لما قالوا من عدم عموم المشترك بل استغناء من المعنيين بأحدهما المتفق عليه سواء كان الحكم مشتركاً لفظياً أو معنوياً. وبهذا يحصل الدفع للإيراد المذكور ولكن ينافي الحمل على هذا المعنى قوله ويكفي في تصحيحه فإنه ظاهر فيما قاله الأصوليون فليتأمل . قوله : (مع أن الإكمل في تقريره أجاب عنه) أي عن الإيراد المذكور وحاصله كما في شرح المنار للشارح أن المشترك المعنوي إن كان متواطئاً قبل العموم وإن كان مشككاً لا يقبله. قوله : (عليهما ) أي على الحكمين قوله : (لكن الثواب والعقاب ليسا كذلك على المذهب (الصحيح أي خلافاً للمعتزلة بل الأعمال عند أهل السنة علامات محضة عليهما كما تقرر في موضعه فإطلاق الحكم عليها يكون بالمعنى الآخر بالضرورة ولا معنى
وقوله إن الوضوء عبادة والعبادة لا تصح إلا بالنية سلمناه لأنه لا يقع عبادة بدونها عندنا وليس الكلام في هذا بل في أنه إذا لم ينو حتى لم يقع عبادة سبباً للثواب فهل يقع الشرط المعتبر للصلاة حتى تصح به أو لا؟ ليس في الحديث دلالة على نفيه ولا إثباته فقلنا لأن الشرط مقصود التحصيل لغيره لا لذاته فكيف حصل حصل المقصود وصار كستر العورة وباقي شروط الصلاة لا يفتقر اعتبارها إلى أن تنوي فمن ادعى أن الشرط وضوء هو

صرح به
عبادة فعليه البيان بخلاف التيمم لأن التراب لم يعتبر شرعاً مطهراً إلا للصلاة وتوابعها لا نفسه فكان التطهير به تعبداً محضاً وفيه يحتاج إلى النية، وقياس الوضوء على التيمم ضعيف لأن شرط صحة القياس أن لا يكون الأصل متأخراً والتيمم شرع بعد الهجرة والوضوء قبلها إلا إن قصد به الاستدلال بمعنى لما شرع التيمم بشرط النية ظهر وجوبها في الوضوء فهو لا فارق فليس الجواب إلا بإثبات الفارق المتقدم، وقد علم النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم الأعرابي الوضوء ولم يبين له النية فلو كانت شرطاً لبينها .له. وقد علم مما قدمناه أن الوضوء يقع عبادة فقول بعضهم إنه ليس بعبادة محمول على ما إذا لم ينو أو مراده نفي العبادة المقصودة كما في الكافي وغيره، وبهذا اندفع ما ذكره النووي من الردّ على من نفي العبادة عن الوضوء بحديث مسلم «الطهور شطر الإيمان (۱) . واعلم أن المذكور في الأصول أن الغسل والمسح في آية الوضوء خاصان وهو لا يحتمل البيان فاشتراط النية في الوضوء زيادة على النص بخبر الواحد لو دل عليها وهو لا يجوز فأورد العقده الأخيرة فإنها فرض بخبر الواحد، فأجيب بأن الصلاة مجملة في حق ما تتم به إذ لم يعرف بأن إتمامها بأي شيء يقع فاحتاج إلى البيان وقد بين بالحديث فالفرض ثبت بالكتاب والحديث التحق به بياناً لمجمله فأورد أنه ينبغي أن يلتحق خبر الفاتحة كذلك، فأجيب بأنه لا إجمال في أمر القراءة بل هو خاص. وأورد أيضاً أنه ينبغي عدم اشتراط النية في العبادات لما ذكر أجيب بأنها فرض فيها لا بالحديث المذكور بل بقوله تعالى وما أمروا إلا ليعبدوا الله مخلصين له الدين) [البينة : ٥] فإنه جعل الإخلاص الذي هو عبارة عن النية حالاً للعابدين والأحوال شروط، ومن هنا نشأ
متمسكاً
للاشتراك إلا هذا قوله : (وقوله أن الوضوء) أي قول الشافعي المفهوم من المقام . قوله : (فقلنا نعم) أي أنه يقع الشرط المعتبر للصلاة. قوله : فليس الجواب إلا بإثبات الفارق المتقدم) وهو أن التراب لم يعتبر شرعاً مطهراً إلا للصلاة قوله : (فمحمول عليه بماء واحد وهو مشروع الخ) قال في فتح القدير : روى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة رضي الله تعالى عنه في المجرد إذا مسح ثلاثاً بماء واحد كان مسنوناً. قوله : (وما قاله بعضهم الخ) أي في كيفية الاستيعاب وبيانه كما ذكره في النهر أن يضع
(۱) رواه مسلم في كتاب الطهارة حديث .١ الترمذي في كتاتب الدعوات باب ٨٦. الدارمي في كتاب الوضوء باب ۲. أحمد في مسنده (٢٦٠/٤).
Book of Purity: The verbal [ambiguity]. As for the common in meaning, it has generality like 'thing' and 'legal ruling' from it, so it encompasses everything by virtue of the broader meaning, since the interpretation of 'legal ruling' is the effect established by the thing. With that the more complete in his presentation answered that this is sound only if the ruling is predicated on both by univocal agreement, which is denied, because permissibility and invalidity, although they are two effects established by actions and rendering them obligatory, but reward and punishment are not like that according to the correct school. That is, because they are not realized in the first due to lack of acceptance of validity, and in the second due to pardon from Allah. By 'actions' is meant what includes the heart, so self-restraint by prohibition enters it, for it is an action. Intention is not rejected because it is excluded for a specific reason: the necessity of infinite regress. But consideration of intention for omissions is only for acquiring reward, not for exiting the obligation of the prohibition, because the basis of threatened punishment in a prohibition is the performance of the prohibited, so mere abandonment suffices for the absence of threat, and the basis of reward in the prohibited is self-restraint from it, which is an action included in the hadith. Based on this, the Shafi'is differentiate between wudu and removal of impurity: wudu is an act so it requires intention, while purification of impurity is of the category of omissions so it does not require intention, like abandoning adultery. This is weak, because obligation always occurs only by the act that is within the capacity of the obligated, not by the non-act which is not capable of existence before the obligation, as known from the implication of prohibition that it is self-restraint from the act, not the non-act. Abandonment is not an act, hence the obligated is not rewarded for omissions unless he abandons intentionally. He is not rewarded for abandoning adultery unless he restrains himself intentionally, not if he is occupied by another act like sleep or worship and abandons it without intention. So there is no difference between act and omission that necessitate reward and punishment. It encompasses both types by verbal homonymy by being placed for each separately? Rather it is common in meaning, assigned for the effect established by the thing, thus it encompasses both rulings, like 'animal' includes human, horse, etc., and 'color' includes black, white, etc. So intending both types is not from the generality of the common at all. There is no need to intend one of them to correct it. You are aware that the presentation presented by the commentator is exactly what the usul scholars presented, so what is objected to them is objected to it. How can the objection be repelled by merely presenting it when there is nothing extra that can serve as a rebuttal, unless it is said: The meaning of his presentation is that we intend by 'ruling' the agreed-upon meaning and leave the other for which there is no evidence, not because of what they said about the lack of generality of the common, but rather dispensing with both meanings by taking the agreed-upon one, whether the ruling is verbally homonymous or common in meaning. By this the repulsion of the objection is achieved, but interpreting it this way contradicts his statement 'and it suffices to correct it', for it is apparent in what the usul scholars said; so let it be considered. His statement: 'while the more complete in his presentation answered about it' i.e., about the mentioned objection. Its summary as in Sharh al-Manar by the commentator: The common in meaning, if it is univocal, accepts generality; if it is graduated, it does not. His statement: 'upon them' i.e., upon the two rulings. His statement: 'but reward and punishment are not like that according to the correct school' i.e., contrary to the Mu'tazila. Rather, actions according to the Ahl al-Sunnah are mere signs for them, as established elsewhere. So applying the term 'ruling' to them is necessarily with the other meaning, and no meaning. And his statement: 'Indeed wudu is worship, and worship is not valid without intention' we accept, because it does not occur as worship without it according to us. But the discussion is not about this; rather it is about whether if one does not intend, so it does not occur as worship meriting reward, does it occur as the valid condition for prayer so that prayer is valid by it or not? The hadith does not indicate its negation nor its affirmation. So we said: Yes, because the condition is intended to be achieved for something else, not for itself. However it is achieved, the objective is achieved, and it becomes like covering the nakedness and the rest of the conditions of prayer, whose consideration does not require that one intend them. So whoever claims that the condition that is wudu is worship must provide evidence. This is contrary to tayammum, because soil has not been legally considered a purifier except for prayer and its dependents, not for itself. So purification by it is purely devotional and requires intention. And analogizing wudu to tayammum is weak, because a condition for the validity of analogy is that the original not later, and tayammum was legislated after the Hijra while wudu was before it, unless it was intended for deduction in the sense that when tayammum was legislated with the condition of intention, its obligation in wudu became apparent. So there is no distinguishing factor, so the answer is only by establishing the previously mentioned distinguishing factor. The Prophet (peace be upon him) taught the Bedouin wudu and did not mention intention to him. So if it were a condition, he would have mentioned it. And from what we have presented, wudu does occur as worship, so the statement of some that it is not worship is interpreted as referring to when one does not intend or they mean denying intended worship, as in al-Kafi and others. By this is repelled what al-Nawawi mentioned in refuting those who deny that wudu is worship by the hadith of Muslim 'Purity is half of faith.' Know that mentioned in usul: The washing and wiping in the verse of wudu are specific and do not admit of interpretation, so prescribing intention in wudu is an addition to the text by a solitary report if it indicates it, which is not permissible. So the objection of the last verse [i.e., 'last sitting'?] was raised, for it is an obligation by a solitary report. It was answered that prayer is ambiguous regarding what completes it, since it is not known by what thing its completion occurs, so it needed clarification, which was provided by the hadith. So the obligation was established by the Book and the attached hadith is a clarification of its ambiguous. Then it was objected that the report of al-Fatiha should attach similarly. It was answered that there is no ambiguity in the matter of recitation, rather it is specific. And also it was objected that intention should not be required in acts of worship for what was mentioned. It was answered that it is obligatory in them not by the mentioned hadith but by His statement: 'And they were commanded not but to worship Allah, being sincere to Him in religion' [98:5], for He made sincerity, which is intention, a state for worshippers, and states are conditions. From here arose a supporter for the commonality except this. His statement: 'And his statement that wudu' means the statement of al-Shafi'i understood from the context. His statement: 'So we said yes' means that it occurs as a valid condition for prayer. His statement: 'So the answer is only by establishing the previously mentioned distinguishing factor' which is that soil has not been legally considered a purifier except for prayer. His statement: 'So it is taken as applicable with one water and it is legislated,' said in Fath al-Qadir: Al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa regarding al-mujarrad: if he wipes three times with one water, it is sunnah. His statement: 'And what some said' refers to how to encompass and explain it as mentioned in al-Nahr: one should place... (hadith reference).

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from Al-Bahr al-Raiq engaging in two interconnected discussions: first, a terminological analysis of the word 'hukm' (legal ruling) and its generality, and second, the main substantive issue of whether intention (niyyah) is required for the validity of wudu (ablution). The commentator is responding to arguments by the Shafi'is and others who assert that niyyah is a condition for wudu. The Hanafi position, as articulated here, is that niyyah is not a condition for the validity of wudu as a prerequisite for prayer (i.e., for the prayer to be valid, the wudu itself does not require niyyah), though niyyah is required for wudu to be considered an act of worship meriting reward. The text begins by discussing how the term 'hukm' can be applied to both permissibility and validity, and to reward and punishment, noting that according to Ahl al-Sunnah, actions are merely signs for reward/punishment, not direct causes. The commentator then moves to the core dispute: the Shafi'is claim that wudu is an act of worship and thus requires niyyah. The Hanafi response is to concede that wudu is worship (in the sense that it earns reward when intended), but to deny that it requires niyyah for its validity as a condition for prayer. Evidence is given: just as covering the nakedness (a condition for prayer) does not require intention, so wudu does not. The Prophet taught a Bedouin wudu without mentioning intention, so if it were a condition, he would have mentioned it. The text distinguishes wudu from tayammum: tayammum is purely devotional and requires niyyah, but wudu is both a condition for prayer and a devotional act. The commentary also addresses objections about adding conditions via solitary reports (akhbar al-ahad). The Hanafi argument is that the verses on wudu (5:6) are specific about washing and wiping and do not admit of addition by a solitary report. However, the obligation of the last sitting in prayer (tashahhud) is established by a solitary report because prayer itself is ambiguous regarding its completion, so the report serves as a clarification (bayan) of a mujmal, which is permissible. In contrast, recitation (qira'a) in prayer is not ambiguous, so a solitary report cannot add it as a requirement. Finally, the commentator refutes the objection that intention is not required for acts of worship by citing the verse 'They were not commanded except to worship Allah with sincere devotion' (98:5), which makes sincerity (a state) a condition. This shows that intention is required for acts of worship, but the Hanafi distinction is that wudu's validity as a condition does not depend on intention. The passage also contains a brief discussion of the method of wiping in wudu, citing a narration from al-Hasan about Abu Hanifa permitting wiping three times with one water as sunnah. Overall, this passage is a dense engagement with usul al-fiqh principles as applied to the specific ruling on wudu, demonstrating how Hanafi jurisprudence uses linguistic analysis, hadith interpretation, and qiyas with istihsan to reach its conclusions.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): Intention, the mental resolve to perform an act of worship for the sake of Allah.
وضوء (wudu): Ritual ablution with water, a condition for prayer.
حكم (hukm): Legal ruling or effect established by a thing; in this passage, discussed as 'atr' (effect).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, is intention (niyyah) required for the validity of wudu as a condition for prayer?
A) Yes, intention is required for all acts of worship.
B) No, intention is not required for validity but only for reward.
C) Yes, intention is required based on the hadith 'al-tuhur shatr al-iman'.
D) No, intention is not required at all, even for reward.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, intention (niyyah) is not required for the validity of wudu as a condition for prayer; it is only required for wudu to be considered an act of worship earning reward.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
12 min
The Necessity of Intention in Wudu: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Debates whether wudu requires niyyah as a condition for prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on intention in wudu and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the hadith of the Bedouin and the nature of wudu as a condition.

Core Idea
Wudu is a condition for prayer, not an act of worship; thus intention is not required for its validity.

This lesson examines the classical dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding whether intention (niyyah) is necessary for the validity of wudu. The Hanafi school maintains that wudu is a condition (shart) for prayer, not an act of worship in itself, so intention is not required. The Shafi'i school argues that wudu is an act of worship and therefore requires intention. We will analyze the evidence presented in the source text and understand the practical implications of this difference.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact Hanafi ruling: wudu performed without intention is valid as a condition for prayer, though it does not earn reward.
The Hanafi school makes a distinction between validity (sihha) and reward (thawab).
2
Identify the opposing Shafi'i view
The Shafi'i school holds that wudu is an act of worship and therefore intention is obligatory for its validity.
3
Examine the Hanafi proof from the hadith of the Bedouin
The Prophet taught wudu to a Bedouin without mentioning intention. If intention were a condition, he would have explained it. This indicates intention is not required.
This hadith is a key dalil for the Hanafi position.
4
Analyze the Hanafi distinction between wudu and tayammum
Tayammum requires intention because it is purely devotional (soil is not inherently purifying). Wudu is different because water is naturally purifying and wudu is a means to an end.
This refutes the analogy that since tayammum requires intention, so should wudu.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
A Hanafi who prays with wudu performed without intention has valid prayer. A Shafi'i would consider the wudu invalid and the prayer null.
This difference has direct impact on daily practice.

وقوله إن الوضوء عبادة والعبادة لا تصح إلا بالنية سلمناه لأنه لا يقع عبادة بدونها عندنا وليس الكلام في هذا بل في أنه إذا لم ينو حتى لم يقع عبادة سبباً للثواب فهل يقع الشرط المعتبر للصلاة حتى تصح به أو لا؟ ليس في الحديث دلالة على نفيه ولا إثباته فقلنا لأن الشرط مقصود التحصيل لغيره لا لذاته فكيف حصل حصل المقصود وصار كستر العورة وباقي شروط الصلاة لا يفتقر اعتبارها إلى أن تنوي فمن ادعى أن الشرط وضوء هو نعم بمعنى في صرح به عبادة فعليه البيان بخلاف التيمم لأن التراب لم يعتبر شرعاً مطهراً إلا للصلاة وتوابعها لا نفسه فكان التطهير به تعبداً محضاً وفيه يحتاج إلى النية، وقياس الوضوء على التيمم ضعيف لأن شرط صحة القياس أن لا يكون الأصل متأخراً والتيمم شرع بعد الهجرة والوضوء قبلها إلا إن قصد به الاستدلال بمعنى لما شرع التيمم بشرط النية ظهر وجوبها في الوضوء فهو لا فارق فليس الجواب إلا بإثبات الفارق المتقدم، وقد علم النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم الأعرابي الوضوء ولم يبين له النية فلو كانت شرطاً لبينها .له. وقد علم مما قدمناه أن الوضوء يقع عبادة فقول بعضهم إنه ليس بعبادة محمول على ما إذا لم ينو أو مراده نفي العبادة المقصودة كما في الكافي وغيره، وبهذا اندفع ما ذكره النووي من الردّ على من نفي العبادة عن الوضوء بحديث مسلم «الطهور شطر الإيمان (۱) . واعلم أن المذكور في الأصول أن الغسل والمسح في آية الوضوء خاصان وهو لا يحتمل البيان فاشتراط النية في الوضوء زيادة على النص بخبر الواحد لو دل عليها وهو لا يجوز فأورد العقده الأخيرة فإنها فرض بخبر الواحد، فأجيب بأن الصلاة مجملة في حق ما تتم به إذ لم يعرف بأن إتمامها بأي شيء يقع فاحتاج إلى البيان وقد بين بالحديث فالفرض ثبت بالكتاب والحديث التحق به بياناً لمجمله فأورد أنه ينبغي أن يلتحق خبر الفاتحة كذلك، فأجيب بأنه لا إجمال في أمر القراءة بل هو خاص. وأورد أيضاً أنه ينبغي عدم اشتراط النية في العبادات لما ذكر أجيب بأنها فرض فيها لا بالحديث المذكور بل بقوله تعالى وما أمروا إلا ليعبدوا الله مخلصين له الدين) [البينة : ٥] فإنه جعل الإخلاص الذي هو عبارة عن النية حالاً للعابدين والأحوال شروط، ومن هنا نشأ متمسكا للاشتراك إلا هذا
And his saying that wudu is worship and worship is not valid except with intention — we concede it, because it does not occur as worship without it according to us. But the discussion is not about this; rather it is about whether, when he does not intend, so it does not occur as worship resulting in reward, does it occur as the valid condition for prayer so that prayer is valid through it, or not? There is no indication in the hadith for negating it nor affirming it. So we said: because a condition is intended to be obtained for something else, not for itself; so however it is obtained, the intended purpose is obtained, and it becomes like covering the 'awrah and the remaining conditions of prayer — their consideration does not require that you intend them. So whoever claims that the condition is wudu — yes, in the sense that he explicitly stated it as worship — must provide proof, contrary to tayammum, because soil is not considered by the Law as purifying except for prayer and its dependents, not itself; thus purification with it is purely devotional, and it requires intention. And analogizing wudu to tayammum is weak, because a condition for the validity of analogy is that the origin should not be later [in revelation], and tayammum was legislated after the Hijra while wudu was before it, unless one intends by it to infer meaning: since tayammum was legislated with the condition of intention, it shows its obligation in wudu. Then there is no difference, so there is no answer except to establish the previously mentioned difference. And the Prophet (peace be upon him) taught the Bedouin wudu and did not explain intention to him; had it been a condition, he would have explained it to him. And it is known from what we have presented that wudu occurs as worship, so the statement of some that it is not worship is interpreted as when he does not intend, or they mean negating intended worship as in al-Kafi and others. With this, refuted is what al-Nawawi mentioned as a refutation against those who negate worship from wudu using the hadith of Muslim: 'Purity is half of faith.' And know that it is mentioned in al-Usul that washing and wiping in the verse of wudu are specific, and they do not admit explanation, so stipulating intention in wudu is an addition to the text by a solitary hadith if it indicates it, and that is not permissible. Then the objection was raised: the last part [recitation], it is obligatory by a solitary hadith. And it was answered: because prayer is ambiguous regarding that by which it is completed, as it is not known by what means its completion occurs, so it needed explanation, and it was explained by the hadith; thus the obligation is established by the Book, and the hadith is joined to it as an explanation of its ambiguity. Then it was objected: the hadith of al-Fatiha should be joined likewise. And it was answered: there is no ambiguity regarding the matter of recitation; rather it is specific. And it was also objected: intention should not be required in acts of worship based on what was mentioned. It was answered: it is obligatory in them not by the mentioned hadith, but by the saying of the Exalted: 'And they were not commanded except to worship Allah, being sincere to Him in religion' [Al-Bayyinah: 5], for He made sincerity, which is an expression of intention, a condition for worshipers, and conditions are prerequisites. From here arose a point of support for treating [intention] as shared [between wudu and other acts], except this.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the necessity of intention (niyyah) for the validity of wudu. The Shafi'i position, inferred from the context, is that wudu is an act of worship ('ibadah) and therefore requires intention. The Hanafi author begins by conceding that wudu can be an act of worship if intended, but the real question is whether wudu without intention is still valid as a condition (shart) for prayer. The Hanafi argument is that wudu, like covering the 'awrah and other conditions of prayer, is a means to an end — it is not an act of worship in itself. Therefore, it does not require intention for its validity. The author then contrasts wudu with tayammum, which is purely devotional because soil is not inherently purifying; hence tayammum requires intention. The analogy of wudu to tayammum is rejected because tayammum was legislated later (after Hijra) and has different characteristics. The primary proof for the Hanafi view is the hadith of the Bedouin, where the Prophet taught wudu without mentioning intention — if intention were a condition, he would have explained it. The author also addresses the objection that wudu is an act of worship by distinguishing between 'worship' in a broad sense and 'intended worship' that earns reward. Finally, the passage engages with usul al-fiqh arguments about whether a solitary hadith can add a condition to a clear Quranic text (the verse of wudu). The Hanafi conclusion is that intention is not obligatory for the validity of wudu, though it is recommended for reward.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): Intention, the mental resolve to perform an act of worship for the sake of Allah. Here it is debated whether it is a condition for wudu.
شرط (shart): A condition; a prerequisite for the validity of an act but not part of its essence. Here wudu is a condition for prayer.
عبادة ('ibadah): An act of worship; an action done specifically to gain reward from Allah. The text discusses whether wudu is an act of worship or merely a means.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on wudu performed without the intention of worship?
A) It is invalid and must be repeated before prayer.
B) It is valid as a condition for prayer but does not earn reward.
C) It is valid only if followed by a deliberate intention before prayer.
D) It is considered makruh and should be repeated.

Key Takeaway
Intention (niyyah) is not required for the validity of wudu according to the Hanafi school, because wudu is a condition (shart) for prayer, not an act of worship in itself.

Wiping the Head Once: The Hanafi Proof and Methodology
States the ruling on head wipe and proves it by hadith and qiyas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wiping the head, cite the primary evidence from the hadith of 'Ali (RA), and explain the qiyas that distinguishes wiping from washing.

Core Idea
The head is wiped once because wiping does not aim at cleaning, unlike washing.

This lesson examines a core ruling of wudu: how many times must you wipe your head? The Hanafi school, based on prophetic practice and careful reasoning, declares that a single comprehensive wipe is obligatory. We will explore the textual evidence, the analogy to other wipes, and the dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and its Ruling
The act is masah (wiping) of the head during wudu. The ruling is that it is wajib to do it once, covering all of the head (isti'ab).
2
Locate the Dalil
The primary proof is the hadith of 'Ali (RA) in al-Tirmidhi, where he demonstrated the Prophet's wudu by washing limbs three times and wiping the head once.
This hadith is ahad, but its transmission is sahih.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
The direct action of 'Ali shows the head wipe is distinct from washing. The absence of repetition for the head indicates that once is sufficient.
The contrast between washing thrice and wiping once is the key.
4
Note the Ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that wiping three times is recommended, analogizing to washing. The Hanafi respond by distinguishing wiped things from washed things.
Al-Shafi'i's qiyas is qiyas al-mamsuh 'ala al-maghsool; Hanafi uses qiyas al-mamsuh 'ala al-mamsuh.
5
Evaluate the Tarjih
The Hanafi position is relied upon (mufta bihi) because it is based on zahir al-riwayah and stronger analogy. The nawadir transmission of wiping three times with same water is considered sunnah, not wajib.
The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq prefers the single wipe.

الغسل ونيته ومسح كل رأسه مرة وأذنيه بمائه والترتيب المنصوص والولاء ومستحبه محله إن شاء الله تعالى . ومسح إشكال على من استدل به على اشتراطها في العبادات كصاحب الهداية مع قولهم في الأصول إن حديث إنما الأعمال بالنيات من قبل ظني الثبوت والدلالة يفيد السنية والاستحباب، وسيأتي تمامه في قوله (ومسح كل رأسه مرة) أي مرة مستوعبة لما روى الترمذي في جامعه أن علياً رضي الله تعالى عنه توضأ وغسل أعضاءه ثلاثاً كيفية المسح والأظهر أن يضع كفيه وأصابعه على مقدّم رأسه ويمدهما إلى القفا على وجه يستوعب جميع الرأس ثم يمسح أذنيه بأصبعيه، ولا يكون الماء مستعملاً بهذا لأن الاستيعاب بماء واحد لا يكون إلا بهذا الطريق. وما قاله بعضهم من أنه يجافي كفيه تحرزاً عن الاستعمال لا يفيد لأنه لا بد من الوضع والمد، فإن كان مستعملاً بالوضع الأول فكذا بالثاني فلا يفيد تأخيره ا هـ . قوله (وأذنيه) بمائه) أي بماء الرأس. وفي يديه ويضع بطون ثلاث أصابع من كل كف على مقدم الرأس ويعزل السبابتين والإبهامين ويجافي الكفين ويجرهما إلى الرأس، ثم يمسح الفودان بالكفين ويجرهما إلى مقدم الرأس، ويمسح ظاهر الأذنين بباطن الإبهامين وباطن Washing, its intention, and wiping all of his head once and his ears with its water, and the prescribed order, and continuity, and its recommended acts — their place, God willing. And wiping: an objection against those who used it to argue for stipulating it in acts of worship, like the author of al-Hidayah, while they say in usul that the hadith 'Indeed actions are by intentions' is zanni in both transmission and meaning, giving only sunnah and recommendation. And its completion will come in his saying: (And wiping all of his head once) i.e., one comprehensive wiping, because al-Tirmidhi narrated in his Jami' that 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) performed wudu, washing his limbs three times and wiping his head once, and said: This is the wudu of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him). And in al-Hidayah: And what is narrated from him, that wiping three times, is interpreted as being done with one water, and it is lawful, as al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifah. End quote. And because repetition in washing is for the sake of thoroughness in cleaning, and that is not achieved by wiping, so repetition is not beneficial; thus it becomes like wiping the khuff, the splint, and tayammum. And what we say is preferable because it is analogizing a wiped thing to a wiped thing, while what al-Shafi'i says is analogizing a wiped thing to a washed thing. And in al-'Inayah: If it is said: the moisture becomes used by the first time, so how is it recommended to pass it over a second and third time? It is answered: it takes the ruling of used moisture for performing another obligatory act due to performing the sunnah, as the sunnah is subsidiary to the obligatory. Do you not see that comprehensive coverage is recommended with one water? And al-Zayla'i said: They discussed the manner of wiping, and the most apparent is that one places his palms and fingers on the front of his head and draws them back to the nape in a manner that covers all of the head, then wipes his ears with his two fingers. The water does not become used by this, because comprehensive coverage with one water is only possible this way. And what some said, that he should separate his palms to avoid using the water, is not beneficial, because placement and drawing back are inevitable; if it becomes used by the first placement, then similarly by the second, so delaying does not help. End quote. His saying: (and his ears) with its water, i.e., with the water of the head. And in al-Mujtaba: He wipes them with his index fingers inside them and with his thumbs outside them, and that is the chosen opinion, as in al-Mi'raj. And from al-Halwani and Shaykh al-Islam: He inserts his little finger into his ears and moves them. And the scholars used as proof the hadith: 'The ears are from the head; they are wiped with what...' He places the inner parts of three fingers of each palm on the front of the head, isolates the index fingers and thumbs, separates the palms, and draws them to the head, then wipes the temples with the palms and draws them to the front of the head, and wipes the outer ears with the inner part of the thumbs and the inner ears with the inner part of the index fingers, and wipes his neck with the outer parts of the hands until he wipes with moisture that did not become used. Thus 'Aishah (may Allah be pleased with her) narrated his wiping (peace and blessings be upon him). End quote. And it is transmitted from al-Hawashi al-Sa'diyyah that his saying 'did not become used' means literally, even if it becomes used in ruling in one limb. His saying: (But if he takes new water...) The implication is that taking new water is required according to us to exit the disagreement so that the act is an act of worship on which there is consensus, but the restriction of the texts that it be with head water indicates that it is sunnah, and likewise their argument using the hadith 'The ears are from the head,' and it is not recommended to renew water for the head, so likewise for what is from it. That (1) reported by Abu Dawud in Kitab al-Taharah, Bab 51; al-Tirmidhi in Kitab al-Taharah, Bab 29; Ibn Majah in Kitab al-Taharah, Bab 53.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the manner of wiping the head (masah) during wudu. The ruling is that the head is wiped once, comprehensively covering the entire head. This is based on the hadith of 'Ali (RA) who demonstrated the Prophet's wudu by washing each limb three times but wiping his head once. The author then explains that some narrations suggest wiping three times, but these are interpreted as being done with a single application of water (i.e., three passes with the same water). The reason for this ruling is that in washing, repetition enhances cleaning, but wiping is not for cleaning in the same way; therefore, repetition does not benefit. Analogy is made to wiping the khuff (leather socks), the splint (jabirah), and tayammum, where a single wipe suffices. The Hanafi position is that wiping the head is obligatory once, and any additional wiping is not required. The passage also discusses the method of wiping: the best practice is to place the palms on the front of the head and draw them back to the nape, covering all of the head, then wipe the ears. The ears are considered part of the head based on the hadith 'الاذنان من الراس' (The ears are from the head). There is also discussion of the used water: moisture on the hand after the first wipe is considered used, but for the purpose of sunnah, it is permissible to use it again for additional wipes, though not recommended. The author concludes that it is sunnah to wipe with the same water of the head, and taking new water for the ears is not recommended, in line with the consensus of the school.

Key Terms
مسح (masah): Wiping a body part with wet hands for purification. In wudu, the head is wiped, not washed.
استيعاب (isti'ab): Comprehensive coverage; ensuring the entire part being wiped is touched.
أذن (udhun): Ear; in wudu, the ears are wiped as part of the head, based on the hadith 'The ears are from the head.'

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how many times should one wipe the head during wudu?
A) Three times, like the washing of the face.
B) Once, comprehensively covering the entire head.
C) Twice, the first and third passes.
D) It depends on the amount of water available.

Key Takeaway
Wiping the head once comprehensively is wajib in the Hanafi school, supported by the hadith of 'Ali and analogy to other acts of wiping.

Wiping the Head Once: Proof and Method
Proof and method for wiping the head once with water.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the number of wipes for the head in wudu, explain the evidence from the hadith of ‘Ali, and distinguish the Hanafi qiyas from the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
The head is wiped once, not thrice, because wiping is not washing and is measured by its own kind.

Wiping the head (masah al-ra’s) is a distinct act in wudu, separate from washing the limbs. While all schools agree that the head must be touched with water, they differ on how many times and whether repetition is recommended. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi position of wiping once, supported by the hadith of ‘Ali (ra) and a consistent analogy with other wipes.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling on head wiping
Identify the ruling: the head is wiped once with water, covering the entire head comprehensively. This is sunnah mu’akkadah, not fard.
Repetition is not recommended; the sunnah is one complete wipe.
2
Examine the primary dalil: the hadith of ‘Ali
Read the hadith narrated by al-Tirmidhi: ‘Ali (ra) washed his limbs thrice and wiped his head once, saying this was the Prophet’s wudu. Consider how this directly indicates the number of wipes.
The hadith is ahad, so its evidence is zanni, but sufficient for a sunnah ruling.
3
Analyze the qiyas: why wiping is not repeated
The Hanafi position is based on qiyas mamsuh ‘ala mamsuh: wiping is analogized to other wipes (khuff, jabeera, tayammum), all of which are done once. Repetition in washing serves cleaning, which wiping does not.
Wiping is for ritual designation, not cleansing.
4
Address the dispute with al-Shafi‘i
Al-Shafi‘i analogizes wiping to washing (qiyas mamsuh ‘ala maghsul), concluding that wiping should be thrice. The Hanafi response: this analogy fails because the purpose and method differ.
The thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafis wipe once, Shafi‘is thrice.
5
Resolve the issue of musta‘mal water
Understand that the moisture from the first wipe is considered musta‘mal, yet the sunnah of comprehensive wiping is performed with that same water because it is subordinate to the fard.
This is a unique Hanafi position that preserves the sunnah without requiring fresh water.

Source Text

ومسح كل رأسه مرة أي مرة مستوعبة لما روى الترمذي في جامعه أن علياً رضي الله تعالى عنه توضأ وغسل أعضاءه ثلاثاً رأسه مرة وقال: هذا وضوء رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم. وفي الهداية : والذي يروى عنه من التثليث فمحمول عليه بماء واحد وهو مشروع على ما روى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة .ا.هـ. ولأن التكرار في الغسل لأجل المبالغة في التنظيف ولا يحصل ذلك بالمسح فلا يفيد التكرار فصار كمسح الخف والجبيرة والتيمم، وما قلناه أولى لأنه قياس الممسوح على الممسوح، وما قال الشافعي قياس الممسوح على المغسول. وفي العناية : فإن قيل قد صار البلل مستعملاً بالمرة الأولى فكيف يسن إمراره ثانياً وثالثاً؟ أجيب بأنه يأخذ حكم الاستعمال لإقامة فرض آخر لإقامة السنة لأنها تبع للفرض، ألا ترى أن الاستيعاب يسن بماء واحد؟ وقال الزيلعي : تكلموا في كيفية المسح والأظهر أن يضع كفيه وأصابعه على مقدّم رأسه ويمدهما إلى القفا على وجه يستوعب جميع الرأس ثم يمسح أذنيه بأصبعيه، ولا يكون الماء مستعملاً بهذا لأن الاستيعاب بماء واحد لا يكون إلا بهذا الطريق. وما قاله بعضهم من أنه يجافي كفيه تحرزاً عن الاستعمال لا يفيد لأنه لا بد من الوضع والمد، فإن كان مستعملاً بالوضع الأول فكذا بالثاني فلا يفيد تأخيره ا هـ .
And wiping all of his head once, i.e., one comprehensive time, because al-Tirmidhi narrated in his Jami‘ that ‘Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, performed wudu and washed his limbs three times, his head once, and said: This is the wudu of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace. And in al-Hidayah: What is reported from him of three times is interpreted as with one water, and it is legislated according to what al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifah, end. And because repetition in washing is for the sake of thorough cleaning, and that is not achieved by wiping, so repetition is not beneficial, so it becomes like wiping the khuff, the splint, and tayammum. And what we said is more appropriate because it is analogizing what is wiped with what is wiped, while what al-Shafi‘i said is analogizing what is wiped with what is washed. And in al-‘Inayah: If it is said: the moisture becomes used (musta‘mal) by the first pass, so how is it recommended to pass it a second and third time? The answer is that it takes the ruling of used water for fulfilling another obligatory act to fulfill the sunnah because it is subordinate to the obligatory act. Do you not see that comprehensive wiping with one water is recommended? And al-Zayla‘i said: They discussed the method of wiping, and the most apparent is that he places his palms and fingers on the front of his head and draws them to the nape in a way that encompasses all of the head, then wipes his ears with his two fingers, and the water does not become used by this because comprehensive wiping with one water is only done in this way. And what some have said about separating his palms to avoid used water is not beneficial because placing and drawing are unavoidable; if it is used by the first placement, then similarly by the second, so delaying it does not help, end.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on wiping the head in wudu: it is performed once comprehensively. The proof is the hadith of ‘Ali (ra) who demonstrated the Prophet’s wudu with three washes for limbs and one for the head. A narration of three wipes is interpreted by Imam Abu Hanifah as using the same water, not three separate wettings. The legal reasoning is that repetition (takrir) benefits washing (ghusl) for cleaning but not wiping (masah), so wiping is analogized to wiping the khuff, splint, and tayammum—all wiped once. This is qiyas mamsuh ‘ala mamsuh, while al-Shafi‘i analogizes wiped to washed, which is rejected. The passage also addresses the concern about water becoming musta‘mal (legally used): the first pass does not render the water used because the subsequent passes are for the sunnah, which is subordinate to the fard. The recommended method is to place palms on the front and draw to the nape, comprehensively. The Hanafi position is that the head is wiped once (not thrice) and this is sufficient for the sunnah.

Key Terms
مسح (masah): Wiping with wet hand over a limb or object; in wudu, specifically wiping the head.
استيعاب (isti‘ab): Comprehensive coverage of the entire head in one continuous wipe.
مستعمل (musta‘mal): Water that has been used in a minor act of worship and is no longer pure for the same act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how many times should the head be wiped in wudu?
A) Once
B) Three times
C) Twice
D) It is not wiped

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school stipulates wiping the head once, not three times, based on the hadith of ‘Ali and a consistent qiyas of mamsuh with mamsuh.

Wiping the Ears: Sunnah with Head Water
Ruling on wiping ears with head water.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wiping the ears in wudu, explain the evidence from hadith, and distinguish it from the Shafi‘i position.

Core Idea
The ears are from the head: wiping them requires no extra water beyond the moisture from the head.

In wudu, the ears are often overlooked. The Hanafi school has a clear position based on hadith: the ears are part of the head for wiping. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the evidence, and the dispute with the Shafi‘i school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? Wiping the ears in wudu. The Hanafi school classifies it as sunnah muakkadah.
It is not fard or wajib; omission does not invalidate wudu.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary evidence is the hadith 'al-udhunani min al-ra's' (the two ears are from the head) and the action of the Prophet who wiped his head and ears with one handful of water.
The hadith is ahad with zanni thubut and dalala.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith explicitly states that the ears are included in the head for wiping, so they require no additional water beyond that used for the head.
The phrase 'yumsahu bimā yumsahu bihi al-ra's' indicates the same water suffices.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi‘i school holds that the ears require fresh water because they consider the remaining moisture from the head as musta‘mal (used).
The dispute is on whether using the same water fulfills the sunnah.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school relies on the apparent meaning of the hadith and reconciles the report of the Prophet taking new water as an exception (wetness exhausted).
The mashayikh and later authorities (e.g., al-Bahr al-Ra’iq) prefer the hadith and conclude that using head water is sufficient.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (وأذنيه) بمائه) أي بماء الرأس. وفي المجتبى يمسحهما بالسبابتين داخلهما وبالإبهامين خارجهما وهو المختار كذا في المعراج وعن الحلواني وشيخ الإسلام: يدخل الخنصر في أذنيه ويحركهما . واستدل المشايخ بالحديث الأذنان من الرأس) يمسحان بما يمسح به الرأس وتمام تقريره في غاية البيان، واستدل في فتح القدير بفعله عليه الصلاة والسلام أنه أخذ غرفة فمسح بها رأسه وأذنيه على ما رواه ابن خزيمة وابن حبان والحاكم. وأما ما روي أنه عليه السلام أخذ لأذنيه ماء جديداً فيجب حمله على أنه لفناء البلة قبل الاستيعاب توفيقاً بينهما مع أنه لو أخذ ماء جديداً من غير فناء البلة كان حسناً كذا في شرح مسكين، فاستفيد منه أن الخلاف بيننا وبين الشافعي في أنه إذا لم يأخذ ماء جديداً أو بالبلة الباقية هل يكون مقيماً للسنة؟ فعندنا نعم، وعنده لا، أما لو أخذ ماء جديداً مع بقاء البلة فإنه يكون مقيماً للسنة اتفاقاً .
His saying: (and his two ears with its water) i.e., with the water of the head. And in al-Mujtaba: he wipes them with the index fingers inside them and with the thumbs outside them, and that is the chosen view, likewise in al-Mi‘raj. And from al-Halwani and Shaykh al-Islam: he inserts the little finger into his ears and moves them. And the mashayikh adduced the hadith: 'The two ears are from the head; they are wiped with what the head is wiped with.' And the full elucidation is in Ghayat al-Bayan. And in Fath al-Qadir, it is adduced by his action, peace be upon him: he took a handful and wiped with it his head and his ears, according to what Ibn Khuzaymah, Ibn Hibban, and al-Hakim narrated. As for what is narrated that he (peace be upon him) took new water for his ears, it must be interpreted as due to the exhaustion of wetness before covering, to reconcile between them, and if he took new water without exhaustion of wetness, it would be good, as in Sharh Miskin. So it is understood from this that the dispute between us and al-Shafi‘i is: if he does not take new water or uses the remaining wetness, does he fulfill the sunnah? According to us, yes; according to him, no. But if he takes new water while wetness remains, then he fulfills the sunnah by agreement.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage details the Hanafi ruling on wiping the ears in wudu. The ears are considered part of the head (al-udhunani min al-ra's) and are wiped with the same water used for the head, not with a separate fresh handful. The recommended method is to wipe the inner ears with the index fingers and the outer ears with the thumbs, or alternatively insert the little fingers. The evidence is the hadith 'The two ears are from the head' and the action of the Prophet (saw) who wiped his head and ears from one handful. A report that he took new water for the ears is reconciled by assuming the moisture from the head had dried before covering, which is an exceptional case. Thus, the Hanafi position is that using the remaining wetness from the head suffices for the sunnah. Al-Shafi‘i holds that one must take new water for the ears, but the Hanafis maintain that the ears share the same water as the head. If one does take new water unnecessarily, it is still valid but not required.

Key Terms
السبابتان (al-sabbābatān): The index fingers, used for wiping the inner ears.
الإبهامان (al-ibhāmān): The thumbs, used for wiping the outer ears.
بلة (bulla): The wetness or moisture remaining on the hand after wiping the head.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on wiping the ears in wudu?
A) Ears must be wiped with new water.
B) Ears are wiped with the same water as the head.
C) Ears are not wiped.
D) Ears must be washed.

Key Takeaway
Wiping the ears is sunnah and is performed with the same water used for the head; no new water is required.
