Proof for Nullification by Blood: Hadith and Qiyas
Providing the key proof from the hadith of Fatima and qiyas for nullification by any impure exit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi proof from the hadith of Fatima and from qiyas that any impure exit from the body nullifies wudu, and explain the conditions for non-sebilan exits.

Core Idea
Any impure exit nullifies wudu; location is irrelevant, but flow ensures true exit.

This passage presents the two primary proofs for the Hanafi ruling that wudu is nullified by any impure substance exiting the body, not only from the front and rear passages. The first proof is the hadith of Fatima bint Abi Hubaysh, which links wudu to blood. The second is qiyas, extending the ruling from the two passages to all exits, with conditions like flow to verify actual exit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling being proved
State that the ruling is that any impure exit from the body nullifies wudu, requiring its renewal for prayer.
This is the operative position (mufta bihi) of the school.
2
Analyze the hadith proof
Examine the hadith of Fatima bint Abi Hubaysh (Bukhari). Identify the key instruction: the Prophet told her to perform wudu for each prayer due to istihadah blood, linking wudu to blood from a vein. This implies that any blood (impurity) exiting the body necessitates wudu.
Hanafis argue that the instruction is part of the hadith, not a later addition by Urwah.
3
Analyze the qiyas proof
Break down the analogical reasoning: Asl (original case) = exit from the two passages with ruling of nullification. Illa (effective cause) = exit of impurity from the body. Far' (branch) = impure exit from any other part. Since the illa is present, the ruling extends.
The specific location is eliminated (tanqih al-manat) as irrelevant.
4
Note the conditions for the branch
For non-sebilan exits, the impurity must flow (sayalan) to a place requiring purification, or for vomiting, fill the mouth. This ensures the impurity truly exits from interior to exterior.
In the two passages, exit is automatically apparent; elsewhere flow confirms exit.
5
Understand the response to objections
Some scholars object: why require flow for branch but not for original? The Hanafi response: in the two passages, exit is inherent; elsewhere flow is needed to confirm exit. For the mouth, it is partly internal, so filling it marks clear exit.
This clarifies the distinction and defends the consistency of the qiyas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذا كله مذهبنا واستدلوا له بأحاديث ضعفها في فتح القدير وأحسن ما يستدل به حديث فاطمة والقياس. أما الأول فما رواه البخاري عن عائشة جاءت فاطمة بنت أبي حبيش إلى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فقالت : يا رسول الله إني امرأة استحاض فلا أطهر أفأدع الصلاة؟ قال : لا إنما ذلك عرق وليست بالحيضة، فإذا أقبلت الحيضة فدعي الصلاة وإذا أدبرت فاغسلي عنك الدم قال هشام بن عروة قال أبي : ثم توضئي لكل صلاة حتى يجيء ذلك الوقت. وما قيل إنه من كلام عروة دفع بأنه خلاف الظاهر لأنه لما كان على مشاكلة الأول لزم كونه من قائل الأول فكان حجة لنا لأنه علل وجوب الوضوء بأنه دم عرق وكل الدماء كذلك. وأما القياس فبيانه أن خروج النجاسة مؤثر في زوال الطهارة شرعاً وقد عقل في الأصل وهو الخارج من السبيلين أن زوال الطهارة عنده وهو الحكم إنما هو بسبب أنه نجس خارج من البدن إذ لم يظهر لكونه من خصوص السبيلين تأثير وقد وجد في الخارج من غيرهما وفيه المناط فيتعدى الحكم إليه، فالأصل الخارج من السبيلين وحكمه زوال الطهارة وعلته خروج النجاسة من البدن وخصوص المحل ملغى، والفرع الخارج النجس من غيرهما وفيه المناط فيتعدى إليه زوال الطهارة التي موجبها الوضوء، فثبت أن موجب هذا القياس ثبوت زوال طهارة الوضوء. وإذا صار زائل الطهارة فعند إرادة الصلاة يتوجه عليه خطاب الوضوء وهو تطهير الأعضاء الأربعة، وإذا صار خروج النجاسة من غير السبيلين كخروجها من السبيلين يرد أن يقال لما اشترطتم في الفرع السيلان أو ملء الفم في القيء مع عدم اشتراطه في الأصل فاجيب بأن النقض بالخروج وحقيقته من الباطن إلى الظاهر وذلك بالظهور في السبيلين يتحقق وفي غيرهما بالسيلان إلى موضع يلحقه التطهير لأن بزوال القشرة تظهر النجاسة في محلها فتكون بادية لا خارجة والفم ظاهر من وجه باطن من وجه فاعتبر ظاهراً في ملء الفم باطناً فيما دونه . قوله (وقيء ملأ فاه) أي وينقضه في ملأ فم المتوضىء. أفرده بالذكر وإن كان داخلاً في الأول لمخالفته في حد الخروج، كذا في التبيين. وإنما لم يفرد الخارج من غير السبيلين
All of this is our madhhab, and they adduced for it hadiths that are considered weak in Fath al-Qadeer, and the best to adduce is the hadith of Fatima and qiyas. As for the first, it is what Bukhari narrated from Aisha: Fatima bint Abi Hubaysh came to the Prophet (peace be upon him) and said, 'O Messenger of Allah, I am a woman with istihadah and I do not become pure; should I leave the prayer?' He said, 'No, that is just a vein and is not menstruation. When the menstrual period comes, leave the prayer, and when it ends, wash the blood from you.' Hisham ibn Urwah said: my father said: 'Then perform wudu for every prayer until that time comes.' And what was said that it is from the speech of Urwah is rebutted as contrary to the apparent meaning, because since it matches the first it must be from the same speaker, so it is a proof for us because he linked the obligation of wudu to blood from a vein, and all blood is like that. As for qiyas, its explanation is that the exit of impurity affects the removal of purity legally, and it is understood in the original case (exit from the two passages) that removal of purity (the ruling) is only because it is impure exiting from the body, since no effect appears due to the particular passage. That cause is found in exit from others, so the ruling extends. The original is exit from the two passages, its ruling is removal of purity, its effective cause is exit of impurity from the body (specific location ignored), and the branch is impure exit from other than the two passages, containing the same cause, so removal of purity required for wudu extends to it. Thus the qiyas establishes removal of purity. When he becomes removed from purity, upon desiring prayer the command of wudu (washing the four limbs) applies to him. If you ask: why did you require in the branch flowing or filling the mouth for vomiting, while not requiring it in the original? The answer is that nullification is by exit, its reality is from interior to exterior; in the two passages that is realized by appearance, while in other places it is realized by flow to a place that is subject to purification, because when the scab is removed, impurity appears in its place, so it is apparent, not exiting. The mouth is external in one way and internal in another, so it is considered external when it fills the mouth, internal for what is below that. His words (and vomiting filling his mouth) mean it nullifies when it fills the mouth of the one performing wudu. It is mentioned separately even though it is included in the first due to its difference in the limit of exit, as in al-Tabyin. And he did not specify exit from other than the two passages alone.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage provides the proof for the Hanafi position that any impure exit from the body nullifies wudu, not only that from the two passages (front and rear). The primary proof is the hadith of Fatima bint Abi Hubaysh (who had istihadah) narrated by Bukhari. The Prophet (PBUH) told her to leave prayer during menstruation but to pray at other times, and after the period ends, she should wash the blood and perform wudu for each prayer. The Hanafis argue that the Prophet linked the obligation of wudu to blood from a vein, implying that any blood exiting the body requires wudu. Although some claim that the instruction to 'perform wudu for every prayer' is from Urwah rather than the Prophet, the Hanafis argue that the context shows it is part of the hadith. The second proof is qiyas: the original case (asl) is exit from the two passages, which causes nullification because of the impure exit. This cause is also present when impurity exits from other parts of the body (the branch), so the ruling extends. However, the Hanafis impose conditions: the impurity must flow to a place requiring purification (which in the two passages occurs naturally) or, for vomiting, fill the mouth because the mouth is partly external. If a scab is removed and blood appears but does not flow, it is not considered exiting. Thus conditions like flow (sayalan) for wounds and fill the mouth (mil' al-fam) for vomiting are applied to ensure the impurity truly exits from the interior to the exterior. The text also clarifies why vomiting is mentioned separately: because its threshold (filling the mouth) differs from the general condition of flow.

Key Terms
استحاضة (istihadah): Non-menstrual uterine bleeding that is pathological, a condition in which blood continues beyond the normal menstrual period.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning: extending a ruling from an original case to a new case based on a shared effective cause.
مناط (manat): The effective cause or rationale that links the ruling to the case.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the qiyas presented in the passage, what is the effective cause (illa) for the nullification of wudu?
A) The specific location of the two passages
B) The exit of impurity from the body
C) The type of impurity (e.g., urine, blood)
D) The amount of impurity

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school proves that any impure exit from the body nullifies wudu using the hadith of Fatima and qiyas, with conditions like flow for non-sebilan sources to ensure true exit.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
10 min
The General Rule: Impure Exits Nullify Wudu
Explains the general nullification by impure exits via qiyas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that any impure exit from the body nullifies wudu and explain the qiyas proof.

Core Idea
Impurity exit from any body part nullifies wudu; the cause is the impurity, not the location.

This passage establishes the foundational Hanafi principle that the exit of impure substances from the body nullifies wudu, even if not from the two private parts. The proof is based on qiyas (analogical reasoning) from the exit from the private parts, where the effective cause is the impurity itself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is the exit of impure substance from the body; the ruling is that it nullifies wudu.
2
Locate the original case (asl)
The original case is the exit from the two private parts (subulayn).
3
Extract the effective cause (illa)
The illa is 'exit of impurity from the body' (khuruj al-najasah min al-badan), regardless of location.
4
Apply qiyas to the new case
The new case (far') is exit from any other body part; since it shares the illa, the ruling transfers.
5
Note the condition for non-private exits
For other exits, flow (sailan) is required for the impurity to be considered 'exiting' (except for vomit where filling the mouth is the indicator).

Book of Purity: [Preference of right side, wiping the neck, shaking it] And it is nullified by impure exit from it, and vomit filling the mouth, even if once, or a clot, or food, or water, or blood predominant over saliva, and [the reason] gathers its scattered parts, and sleeping lying on side or sitting cross-legged, contrary to exit from them as in al-Wafi because flow is derived from exit as we have mentioned, unlike filling the mouth. The proof for our madhhab has preceded, and it is the madhhab of the ten who were given glad tidings of Paradise and those who followed them. There is disagreement over the definition of filling the mouth: in al-Mi'raj and others it is corrected as that which cannot be held except with difficulty, and in al-Yanabi' it is corrected as that which one cannot hold. Its justification is that then the impurity exits visibly because this vomit is only from the bottom of the stomach, so it apparently carries impurity, unlike a small amount which is from the top of the stomach and does not carry it. And because the mouth has cavities considered legally so that if a fasting person swallows his saliva, his fast is not broken, just as if impurity moves from one place to another inside the body, and outwardly so that inserting water does not break the fast. So we consider both aspects: a small amount does not nullify due to considering the cavities, and a large amount nullifies due to impurity exiting visibly. His statement (And even if once or a clot or food or water) is an explanation that there is no difference between types of vomit. A clot is something intensely red and coagulated. The same applies to food and water. Al-Hasan said: If one consumes food or water and then vomits it immediately, it does not nullify because it is pure since it has not changed, and only a small amount of vomit is attached to it, so it is not an impurity event. Similarly, a child who suckles and vomits immediately—al-Mi'raj and others authenticated it. The point of disagreement is when it reaches his stomach and does not settle. But if he vomits before reaching it, while it is in the esophagus, it does not nullify by agreement, as al-Zahidi mentioned. In Fath al-Qadir: If one vomits many worms or a snake filling his mouth, it does not nullify because what is attached to it is little and it is not a nullifier. End quote. It may be said: It should be, according to the one who rules that the worm is impure, that it nullifies if it fills the mouth. Or his statement (not phlegm) is a conjunction to 'once' i.e., phlegm does not nullify. He stated it generally, so it includes whether it is from the head or chest, filling the mouth or not, mixed with food or not, except if the food fills the mouth. According to Abu Yusuf: phlegm rising from the chest nullifies if it fills the mouth like other types of vomit because it becomes impure in the stomach by adjacency, unlike the descending from the head, as it is not a place of impurity. According to them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad): it is viscous and shiny, particles of impurity do not penetrate it, so it is like saliva, and what attaches to it from vomit is little, and the case where phlegm falls into impurity is not considered because our discussion is when it is inside. But when it separates, its thickness decreases and its thinness increases, and [the ruling] accepts it? This is in many books, and it is apparent that phlegm is not...
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage is a detailed legal commentary on nullification of wudu by impure substances exiting the body from other than the two private parts. It begins by affirming the Hanafi position that such exit nullifies wudu, proven by qiyas (analogical reasoning) from the two private parts. The key condition for nullification is actual exit (khuruj), which in the case of vomit is defined by 'filling the mouth' (mil' al-fam), because the mouth is partly internal and partly external. The commentator then addresses specific issues: the definition of mil' al-fam (preferred: cannot hold except with difficulty), types of vomit (once, clot, food, water — all alike), and the ruling on phlegm (balgham): it does not nullify according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad due to its viscosity, but Abu Yusuf rules it nullifies if it rises from the chest and fills the mouth. The passage also includes a significant intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the nullification by squeezing a sore (asr al-qarha). Some Hanafi scholars (like in al-Zahiriya and al-Hidaya) say it does not nullify because the exit is not natural (bil-tab'), while others (al-Tatimma, al-Khulasa, al-Kafi, al-Sarakhsi) argue it does, drawing an analogy to cupping (hijama) and phlebotomy (fasd). The commentator (al-Ramli) supports the view that squeezing also nullifies because the exit of impurity occurs, and the effective cause is the impurity itself, not the manner of exit. The passage also notes that vomiting many worms does not nullify because what attaches is little, unless one rules worms impure. Overall, this is a classic Sharh (expansion) that clarifies the source text's rulings with proofs, definitions, and ikhtilaf.

Key Terms
ملء الفم (mil' al-fam): The amount of vomit that fills the mouth, defined as that which cannot be held except with difficulty or cannot be held at all.
القيء (al-qay'): Vomit; if it fills the mouth, it nullifies wudu regardless of type (food, water, clot, etc.).
البلغم (al-balgham): Phlegm; considered not nullifying by the majority of Hanafis because it does not carry impurity like saliva.
العصر (al-'asr): Squeezing a sore or wound to cause blood or pus to exit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi qiyas, what is the effective cause (illa) that transfers the ruling of nullification from the private parts to other body parts?
A) The specific location of the exit
B) The exit of impurity from the body
C) The presence of blood
D) The flow of liquid

Key Takeaway
Any impure exit from the body nullifies wudu, proven by qiyas from the private parts, provided it flows (or fills the mouth for vomit).
